## μάγος (id: 003120000000000)

μάγος
=====

μάγος (G3097)

noun \| \-ου \| μαγεύω

32\.40 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

a wise man and priest, a magus a person noted for unusual capacity of understanding based upon astrology (such persons were regarded as combining both secular and religious aspects of knowledge and understanding)1 In [MAT 2:1](https://ref.ly/Matt2:1) μάγοι may be translated as ‘men of wisdom who studied the stars.’

[MAT 2:1](https://ref.ly/Matt2:1) · [MAT 2:7](https://ref.ly/Matt2:7) · [MAT 2:16](https://ref.ly/Matt2:16) · [MAT 2:16](https://ref.ly/Matt2:16)

53\.97 · Religious Activities · Magic

magician (derivative of μαγεύω ‘to practice magic,’ [53\.96](#53.96)) one who practices magic and witchcraft

[ACT 13:6](https://ref.ly/John13:6) · [ACT 13:8](https://ref.ly/John13:8)

1 It would also be possible to classify μάγος in Domain 28 Know, in view of the highly specialized knowledge involved. Because of the religious implications of the role of a μάγος, this term is also classified under Domain 53 Religious Activities (see [53\.97](#53.97)). But the dominant semantic feature of μάγος a would seem to be reputed wisdom, and therefore it is treated in this domain, Understand (32\).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 2:1; Matthew 2:7; Matthew 2:16; Acts 13:6; Acts 13:8

## μαθητεύω (id: 003123000000000)

μαθητεύω
========

μαθητεύω (G3100)

μαθητής · μαθήτρια · συμμαθητής

36\.31 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Follow, Be a Disciple

to follow, to be a disciple of to be a follower or a disciple of someone, in the sense of adhering to the teachings or instructions of a leader and in promoting the cause of such a leader Though many translators have attempted to employ the metaphorical significance of ‘to follow’ in the sense of ‘to be a disciple of,’ there are certain dangers in a number of languages. For example, ‘to follow’ may often have the connotation of ‘to pursue after with evil intent.’ In many languages the appropriate equivalent of ‘to follow’ (in the sense of ‘to be a disciple’) is literally ‘to accompany’ or ‘to go along with’ or ‘to be in the group of.’

[MAT 13:52](https://ref.ly/Matt13:52) · [MAT 27:57](https://ref.ly/Matt27:57)

36\.37 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Follow, Be a Disciple

to make disciples, to cause people to become followers to cause someone to become a disciple or follower of In rendering μαθητεύω in [MAT 28:19](https://ref.ly/Matt28:19) and similar contexts, it is important to avoid the implication of duress or force, that is to say, one should not translate ‘force them to be my disciples’ or ‘compel them to be my disciples.’ This might very well be implied in a literal translation of a causative such as ‘to make.’ In order to avoid a wrong implication of a causative, it may be important to use some such expression as ‘convince them to become my disciples’ or ‘urge them to be my disciples.’

[MAT 28:19](https://ref.ly/Matt28:19) · [ACT 14:21](https://ref.ly/John14:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:52; Matthew 27:57; Matthew 28:19; Acts 14:21


## μαθητής (id: 003124000000000)

μαθητής
=======

μαθητής (G3101)

noun \| \-οῦ \| μαθητεύω

36\.38 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Follow, Be a Disciple

disciple, follower (derivative of μαθητεύω\[a] ‘to follow, to be a disciple of,’ [36\.31](#36.31)) a person who is a disciple or follower of someone Though in the NT μαθητής generally refers to men, it is neutral as to sex distinction, and thus in a few instances in the NT also includes women (as in [ACT 6:1](https://ref.ly/John6:1), πληθυνόντων τῶν μαθητῶν ‘the number of disciples kept growing’). In some languages it may be important to indicate clearly the sex distinction, and in those contexts in which the twelve disciples are being referred to, obviously the reference must be to men. However, when the wider group of disciples is referred to, then some indication should be introduced as to the fact that both men and women were involved.

20:1](https://ref.ly/John20:1) · [ACT 20:30](https://ref.ly/John20:30) · [ACT 21:4](https://ref.ly/John21:4) · [ACT 21:16](https://ref.ly/John21:16) · [ACT 21:16](https://ref.ly/John21:16)

27\.16 · Learn · Learn

disciple, pupil (derivative of μανθάνω\[a] ‘to learn, to be instructed,’ [27\.12](#27.12)) a person who learns from another by instruction, whether formal or informal1

[LUK 6:40](https://ref.ly/Mark6:40)

## μαίνομαι (id: 003130000000000)

========

ἐμμαίνομαι · μανία

30\.24 · Think · To Think, Thought

to not be in one’s right mind, to be insane, to be mad, to be out of one’s mind, insanity, madness to think or reason in a completely irrational manner1

[JHN 10:20](https://ref.ly/Luke10:20) · [ACT 12:15](https://ref.ly/John12:15) · [ACT 26:24](https://ref.ly/John26:24) · [ACT 26:25](https://ref.ly/John26:25) · [1CO 14:23](https://ref.ly/Rom14:23)

## μακαρισμός (id: 003133000000000)

μακαρισμός
==========

μακαρισμός (G3108)

noun \| \-οῦ \| μακαρίζω

25\.118 · Attitudes and Emotions · Happy, Glad, Joyful

happiness a state of happiness, implying favorable circumstances In [GAL 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:15) μακαρισμός clearly refers to a state of happiness which occurred in the past but which was no longer evident. It may therefore be necessary to indicate that the happiness in question is past, and accordingly, one may translate ‘you were so happy! What has happened?’ or ‘then you were so happy! What has happened to you now?’

[ROM 4:6](https://ref.ly/Acts4:6) · [ROM 4:9](https://ref.ly/Acts4:9) · [GAL 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 4:6; Romans 4:9; Galatians 4:15

88\.281 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

homosexual the passive male partner in homosexual intercourse For a context of μαλακός\[b], see [1CO 6:9](https://ref.ly/Rom6:9) in [88\.280](#88.280). As in Greek, a number of other languages also have entirely distinct terms for the active and passive roles in homosexual intercourse.

[1CO 6:9](https://ref.ly/Rom6:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:8; Luke 7:25; 1 Corinthians 6:9

## μάμμη (id: 003150000000000)

μάμμη
=====

μάμμη (G3125)

noun \| \-ης

10\.19 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

grandmother the mother of one’s own mother or father (with a possible connotation of affection) In a number of languages it is necessary to distinguish between the grandmother on one’s father’s side and the grandmother on one’s mother’s side. There is no positive indication in [2TI 1:5](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:5) as to the particular relationship involved, but one may assume that the grandmother Lois was the mother of Eunice, and therefore it would be the grandmother on the mother’s side.

[2TI 1:5](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:5)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Timothy 1:5

## μανθάνω (id: 003154000000000)

μανθάνω
=======

μανθάνω (G3129)

aor. ἔμαθον · inf. μαθεῖν · pf. μεμάθηκα \| ἀμαθής · καταμανθάνω

27\.12 · Learn · Learn

to learn, to be instructed, to be taught to acquire information as the result of instruction, whether in an informal or formal context

[MAT 11:29](https://ref.ly/Matt11:29) · [MAT 24:32](https://ref.ly/Matt24:32) · [MRK 13:28](https://ref.ly/Matt13:28) · [JHN 6:45](https://ref.ly/Luke6:45) · [JHN 7:15](https://ref.ly/Luke7:15)1 · [ACT 23:27](https://ref.ly/John23:27) · [ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) · [1CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/Rom4:6) · [1CO 14:31](https://ref.ly/Rom14:31) · [1CO 14:35](https://ref.ly/Rom14:35) · [GAL 3:2](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:2) · [EPH 4:20](https://ref.ly/Gal4:20) · [PHP 4:9](https://ref.ly/Eph4:9) · [COL 1:7](https://ref.ly/Phil1:7) · [1TI 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:11) · [1TI 5:4](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:4) · [1TI 5:13](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:13) · [2TI 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:7) · [2TI 3:14](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:14) · [2TI 3:14](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:14) · [TIT 3:14](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:14) · [REV 14:3](https://ref.ly/Jude14:3)

27\.15 · Learn · Learn

to learn, to come to realize to learn from experience, often with the implication of reflection

[MAT 9:13](https://ref.ly/Matt9:13) · [PHP 4:11](https://ref.ly/Eph4:11) · [HEB 5:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:8)

32\.14 · Understand · Come To Understand

to understand to come to understand as the result of a process of learning It is possible to understand μανθάνω in [1CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/Rom4:6) as meaning simply ‘to learn’ (see [27\.12](#27.12)).

[1CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/Rom4:6)

1 JHN 7:15 A translation of [JHN 7:15](https://ref.ly/Luke7:15) which merely says ‘when he has never been to school’ gives quite a wrong impression, for Jesus undoubtedly did attend a local synagogue school where he learned to read and write and studied the Scriptures. What is implied in [JHN 7:15](https://ref.ly/Luke7:15) is that Jesus was not the disciple of a particular rabbi nor did he have formal or advanced instruction under a recognized rabbi.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:29; Matthew 24:32; Mark 13:28; John 6:45; John 7:15; Acts 23:27; Romans 16:17; 1 Corinthians 4:6; 1 Corinthians 14:31; 1 Corinthians 14:35; Galatians 3:2; Ephesians 4:20; Philippians 4:9; Colossians 1:7; 1 Timothy 2:11; 1 Timothy 5:4; 1 Timothy 5:13; 2 Timothy 3:7; 2 Timothy 3:14; Titus 3:14; Revelation 14:3; Matthew 9:13; Philippians 4:11; Hebrews 5:8


## μανία (id: 003155000000000)

μανία
=====

μανία (G3130)

noun \| \-ας \| μαίνομαι

30\.24 · Think · To Think, Thought

to not be in one’s right mind, to be insane, to be mad, to be out of one’s mind, insanity, madness to think or reason in a completely irrational manner1 In some languages μανία is best rendered by an idiomatic expression, for example, ‘thoughts that never return,’ ‘distorted thoughts,’ ‘senseless thoughts,’ or ‘thoughts that cannot be understood.’

[ACT 26:24](https://ref.ly/John26:24)

1 It is possible that there are some significant differences in meaning between the set μαίνομαι / μανία and the set παραφρονέω / παραφρονία, but the difference is likely to be more connotative than denotative, as, for example, the distinction in English between crazy and insane.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 26:24


## μάννα (id: 003156000000000)

μάννα
=====

μάννα (G3131)

noun

5\.22 · Foods and Condiments · Food

manna the miraculous food given by God to the Israelites during their journey through the wilderness In most languages μάννα is rendered by a transliteration as ‘manna’ or ‘mana.’ One must, however, be very careful about the transliteration of this term, since it may correspond to an indigenous expression having quite a different meaning. Although in the OT it may be useful to have a marginal note explaining the play on words involved in the derivation of this term, in the NT one can usually use an expression such as ‘food called manna.’

[JHN 6:31](https://ref.ly/Luke6:31) · [JHN 6:49](https://ref.ly/Luke6:49) · [HEB 9:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:4) · [REV 2:17](https://ref.ly/Jude2:17)

* **Associated Passages:** John 6:31; John 6:49; Hebrews 9:4; Revelation 2:17


## μαντεύομαι (id: 003157000000000)

μαντεύομαι
==========

μαντεύομαι (G3132)

33\.284 · Communication · Foretell, Tell Fortunes

to tell fortunes to function as a more or less professional predicter of future events for the sake of a fee In [ACT 16:16](https://ref.ly/John16:16) μαντεύομαι may often be translated as ‘for money she told people what was going to happen to them.’

[ACT 16:16](https://ref.ly/John16:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 16:16


## μαραίνω (id: 003158000000000)

μαραίνω
=======

μαραίνω (G3133) — μαραίνομαι

ἀμαράντινος · ἀμάραντος

13\.94 · (μαραίνομαι) · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Exist

to fade away to go out of existence gradually In many languages it is simply not possible to speak of a ‘rich man fading away.’ Colors may fade, but not a person, and therefore it may be necessary to shift the figure of speech, for example, ‘the rich man will end up being no one’ or ‘the rich man will finally count for nothing.’

[JAS 1:11](https://ref.ly/Heb1:11)

* **Associated Passages:** James 1:11


## μαράνα θᾶ (id: 003159000000000)

μαράνα θᾶ
=========

μαράνα θᾶ (G3134) — θα, μαρανα, μαρανα θα

12\.11 · (μαρανα) · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

our Lord (an Aramaic word) The expression μαρανα θα in [1CO 16:22](https://ref.ly/Rom16:22) is an Aramaic formula evidently associated with early Christian liturgy. It must have been widely used, since it occurs in [1CO 16:22](https://ref.ly/Rom16:22) without explanation.

[1CO 16:22](https://ref.ly/Rom16:22)

15\.82 · (θα) · Linear Movement · Come, Come To, Arrive

to come (an Aramaic word) to move to or toward a reference point of the viewpoint character or event1

[1CO 16:22](https://ref.ly/Rom16:22)

1 In the Didache (10,6\) and in some NT manuscripts the expression reads μαραν αθα (our) Lord has come.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 16:22


## μαργαρίτης (id: 003160000000000)

μαργαρίτης
==========

μαργαρίτης (G3135)

noun \| \-ου

2\.43 · Natural Substances · Precious and Semiprecious Stones and Substances

pearl a smooth, rounded concretion formed within the shells of certain mollusks and valued as a gem because of its lustrous color (see [2\.29](#2.29)) In general there is little difficulty involved in obtaining a satisfactory term for ‘pearl,’ since such objects are relatively well known throughout the world. However, in some languages there is no term for ‘pearl,’ and therefore one may use in the case of [REV 21:21](https://ref.ly/Jude21:21) ‘beautiful white stones,’ and in [MAT 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6) it may be appropriate to translate ‘do not throw your valuable jewels to pigs.’

[MAT 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6) · [MAT 13:45](https://ref.ly/Matt13:45) · [MAT 13:46](https://ref.ly/Matt13:46) · [1TI 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:9) · [REV 17:4](https://ref.ly/Jude17:4) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) · [REV 18:16](https://ref.ly/Jude18:16) · [REV 21:21](https://ref.ly/Jude21:21) · [REV 21:21](https://ref.ly/Jude21:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:6; Matthew 13:45; Matthew 13:46; 1 Timothy 2:9; Revelation 17:4; Revelation 18:12; Revelation 18:16; Revelation 21:21

noun \| \-ου

2\.45 · Natural Substances · Precious and Semiprecious Stones and Substances

marble a colorful, relatively hard form of limestone which may be polished to a lustrous finish (especially valued as material for building or for sculpture) Where there is no technical term for ‘marble,’ one may use an expression such as ‘beautiful rock’ or ‘valuable stone.’

## μαρτυρία (id: 003166000000000)

μαρτυρία
========

μαρτυρία (G3141)

noun \| \-ας \| μαρτυρέω

33\.262 · Communication · Witness, Testify

to witness to provide information about a person or an event concerning which the speaker has direct knowledge In a number of languages it is necessary to indicate specifically what is the content of a witness, so that, for example, in [LUK 21:13](https://ref.ly/Mark21:13) it may be necessary to say ‘this is your chance to witness to the good news’ or ‘... to tell about the good news’ or ‘... to tell what you yourselves know about the good news.’

[LUK 22:71](https://ref.ly/Mark22:71) · [JHN 1:7](https://ref.ly/Luke1:7) · [ACT 22:18](https://ref.ly/John22:18)

33\.264 · Communication · Witness, Testify

testimony, witness (derivative of μαρτυρέω\[a] ‘to witness,’ [33\.262](#33.262)) the content of what is witnessed or said In a number of languages one must specify the content of the witness, and it also may be necessary to indicate the agent who is engaged in the witnessing. For example, in [MRK 14:55](https://ref.ly/Matt14:55) it may be necessary to translate ‘they tried to find someone who would testify against Jesus’ or ‘... say something against Jesus.’ In [1CO 1:6](https://ref.ly/Rom1:6) it may be necessary to translate ‘what we told you from personal experience about Christ has become so firmly fixed in you’ or ‘... has become so much a part of you.’

[MRK 14:55](https://ref.ly/Matt14:55) · [MRK 14:56](https://ref.ly/Matt14:56) · [MRK 14:59](https://ref.ly/Matt14:59) · [JHN 1:19](https://ref.ly/Luke1:19) · [JHN 3:11](https://ref.ly/Luke3:11) · [JHN 3:32](https://ref.ly/Luke3:32) · [JHN 3:33](https://ref.ly/Luke3:33) · [JHN 5:31](https://ref.ly/Luke5:31) · [JHN 5:32](https://ref.ly/Luke5:32) · [JHN 5:34](https://ref.ly/Luke5:34) · [JHN 5:36](https://ref.ly/Luke5:36) · [JHN 8:13](https://ref.ly/Luke8:13) · [JHN 8:14](https://ref.ly/Luke8:14) · [JHN 8:17](https://ref.ly/Luke8:17) · [JHN 19:35](https://ref.ly/Luke19:35) · [JHN 21:24](https://ref.ly/Luke21:24) · [TIT 1:13](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:13) · [1JN 5:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:9) · [1JN 5:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:9) · [1JN 5:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:9) · [1JN 5:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:10) · [1JN 5:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:10) · [1JN 5:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:11) · [3JN 1:12](https://ref.ly/2John1:12) · [REV 1:2](https://ref.ly/Jude1:2) · [REV 1:9](https://ref.ly/Jude1:9) · [REV 6:9](https://ref.ly/Jude6:9) · [REV 11:7](https://ref.ly/Jude11:7) · [REV 12:11](https://ref.ly/Jude12:11) · [REV 12:17](https://ref.ly/Jude12:17) · [REV 19:10](https://ref.ly/Jude19:10) · [REV 19:10](https://ref.ly/Jude19:10) · [REV 20:4](https://ref.ly/Jude20:4)

33\.265 · Communication · Witness, Testify

reputation (derivative of μαρτυρέω\[b] to speak well of, [33\.263](#33.263)) that which is said about a person on the basis of an evaluation of the persons conduct In obtaining a satisfactory equivalent for ‘reputation,’ it may be necessary to restructure considerably the clause in which a term such as μαρτυρία\[c] or ὄνομα\[c] occurs. For example, in [1TI 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:7) one may translate ‘he should be the kind of man that people outside the church say is a good person.’ Similarly, in [REV 3:1](https://ref.ly/Jude3:1) one may need to translate ‘people speak of you as being alive even though you are dead.’

[1TI 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 22:71; John 1:7; Acts 22:18; Mark 14:55; Mark 14:56; Mark 14:59; John 1:19; John 3:11; John 3:32; John 3:33; John 5:31; John 5:32; John 5:34; John 5:36; John 8:13; John 8:14; John 8:17; John 19:35; John 21:24; Titus 1:13; 1 John 5:9; 1 John 5:10; 1 John 5:11; 3 John 1:12; Revelation 1:2; Revelation 1:9; Revelation 6:9; Revelation 11:7; Revelation 12:11; Revelation 12:17; Revelation 19:10; Revelation 20:4; 1 Timothy 3:7

## μάρτυς (id: 003169000000000)

noun \| μάρτυρος · dat.pl. μάρτυσιν \| μαρτυρέω

33\.270 · Communication · Witness, Testify

witness, one who testifies (derivative of μαρτυρέω\[a] ‘to witness,’ [33\.262](#33.262)) a person who witnesses

[MAT 18:16](https://ref.ly/Matt18:16) · [MAT 26:65](https://ref.ly/Matt26:65) · [MRK 14:63](https://ref.ly/Matt14:63) · [LUK 11:48](https://ref.ly/Mark11:48) · [LUK 24:48](https://ref.ly/Mark24:48) · [ACT 1:8](https://ref.ly/John1:8) · [ACT 1:22](https://ref.ly/John1:22) · [ACT 2:32](https://ref.ly/John2:32) · [ACT 3:15](https://ref.ly/John3:15) · [ACT 5:32](https://ref.ly/John5:32) · [ACT 6:13](https://ref.ly/John6:13) · [ACT 7:58](https://ref.ly/John7:58) · [ACT 10:39](https://ref.ly/John10:39) · [ACT 10:41](https://ref.ly/John10:41) · [ACT 13:31](https://ref.ly/John13:31) · [ACT 22:15](https://ref.ly/John22:15) · [ACT 26:16](https://ref.ly/John26:16) · [ROM 1:9](https://ref.ly/Acts1:9) · [2CO 1:23](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:23) · [2CO 13:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor13:1) · [PHP 1:8](https://ref.ly/Eph1:8) · [1TH 2:5](https://ref.ly/Col2:5) · [1TH 2:10](https://ref.ly/Col2:10) · [1TI 5:19](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:19) · [1TI 6:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:12) · [2TI 2:2](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:2) · [HEB 10:28](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:28) · [HEB 12:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:1) · [1PE 5:1](https://ref.ly/Jas5:1) · [REV 1:5](https://ref.ly/Jude1:5) · [REV 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jude2:13) · [REV 3:14](https://ref.ly/Jude3:14) · [REV 11:3](https://ref.ly/Jude11:3)

20\.67 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Kill

martyr a person who has been deprived of life as the result of bearing witness to his beliefs A strictly literal translation of the Greek expression in [REV 17:6](https://ref.ly/Jude17:6) (ἐκ τοῦ αἵματος τῶν μαρτύρων Ἰησοῦ ‘of the blood of the martyrs of Jesus’) is likely to result in considerable misunderstanding, for it could mean that these were individuals who had been martyred by Jesus rather than those who had been deprived of their lives because of their relationship to Jesus. It would be possible to render τῶν μαρτύρων Ἰησοῦ as ‘those who had been killed because they belonged to Jesus,’ but one should avoid any expression which would suggest slave ownership.

[ACT 22:20](https://ref.ly/John22:20) · [REV 17:6](https://ref.ly/Jude17:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 18:16; Matthew 26:65; Mark 14:63; Luke 11:48; Luke 24:48; Acts 1:8; Acts 1:22; Acts 2:32; Acts 3:15; Acts 5:32; Acts 6:13; Acts 7:58; Acts 10:39; Acts 10:41; Acts 13:31; Acts 22:15; Acts 26:16; Romans 1:9; 2 Corinthians 1:23; 2 Corinthians 13:1; Philippians 1:8; 1 Thessalonians 2:5; 1 Thessalonians 2:10; 1 Timothy 5:19; 1 Timothy 6:12; 2 Timothy 2:2; Hebrews 10:28; Hebrews 12:1; 1 Peter 5:1; Revelation 1:5; Revelation 2:13; Revelation 3:14; Revelation 11:3; Acts 22:20; Revelation 17:6

## μαστός (id: 003174000000000)

μαστός
======

μαστός (G3149)

noun \| \-οῦ

8\.37 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

breast the breast of both humans and animals, with special reference to the mammary glands In [REV 1:13](https://ref.ly/Jude1:13) the phrase πρὸς τοῖς μαστοῖς is a reference to the particular location of the gold band which went around the chest and not to the mammary glands as such. In some languages, therefore, it is often preferable to use a phrase such as ‘around his chest’ rather than trying to be more specific, for example, ‘a gold band around his chest at the location of his breasts.’  
In translating [LUK 11:27](https://ref.ly/Mark11:27) it is important to use an expression which will be perfectly natural, for example, ‘the breasts that gave you milk’ or ‘the breasts from which you obtained milk.’ In some instances, however, a specific reference to breasts as the source of milk may seem somewhat vulgar, and therefore it may be better to speak of ‘happy is your mother who nursed you.’

[LUK 11:27](https://ref.ly/Mark11:27) · [LUK 23:29](https://ref.ly/Mark23:29) · [REV 1:13](https://ref.ly/Jude1:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 11:27; Luke 23:29; Revelation 1:13

## μάχαιρα (id: 003184000000000)

μάχαιρα
=======

μάχαιρα (G3162)

noun \| \-ης

6\.33 · Artifacts · Weapons and Armor

sword, dagger a relatively short sword (or even dagger) used for cutting and stabbing The phrase στόμα μαχαίρης (literally ‘mouth of the sword’) refers to the event of killing or slaughter: ἔφυγον στόματα μαχαίρης ‘they escaped being killed by the sword’ [HEB 11:34](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:34). See [79\.109](#79.109).

[MAT 26:47](https://ref.ly/Matt26:47) · [MAT 26:51](https://ref.ly/Matt26:51) · [MAT 26:52](https://ref.ly/Matt26:52) · [MAT 26:52](https://ref.ly/Matt26:52) · [MAT 26:52](https://ref.ly/Matt26:52) · [MAT 26:55](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55) · [MRK 14:43](https://ref.ly/Matt14:43) · [MRK 14:47](https://ref.ly/Matt14:47) · [MRK 14:48](https://ref.ly/Matt14:48) · [LUK 21:24](https://ref.ly/Mark21:24) · [LUK 22:36](https://ref.ly/Mark22:36) · [LUK 22:38](https://ref.ly/Mark22:38) · [LUK 22:49](https://ref.ly/Mark22:49) · [LUK 22:52](https://ref.ly/Mark22:52) · [JHN 18:10](https://ref.ly/Luke18:10) · [JHN 18:11](https://ref.ly/Luke18:11) · [ACT 12:2](https://ref.ly/John12:2) · [ACT 16:27](https://ref.ly/John16:27) · [EPH 6:17](https://ref.ly/Gal6:17) · [HEB 4:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:12) · [HEB 11:34](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:34) · [HEB 11:37](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:37) · [REV 6:4](https://ref.ly/Jude6:4) · [REV 13:10](https://ref.ly/Jude13:10) · [REV 13:10](https://ref.ly/Jude13:10) · [REV 13:14](https://ref.ly/Jude13:14)

war, fighting, conflict (figurative extension of meaning of μάχαιρα\[a] ‘sword,’ [6\.33](#6.33)) For another interpretation of μάχαιρα in [MAT 10:34](https://ref.ly/Matt10:34), see [39\.25](#39.25).

## μάχη (id: 003185000000000)

μάχη
====

μάχη (G3163)

noun \| \-ης \| μάχομαι

39\.23 · Hostility, Strife · Strife, Struggle

severe clash, struggle, fight serious conflict, either physical or non\-physical, but clearly intensive and bitter In order to suggest something of the intensity of conflict in μάχομαι and μάχη, it may be useful in some instances to employ similes in the rendering of these terms, for example, ‘they opposed one another just as though they were actually fighting one another’ or ‘they are fighting, as it were.’

[2CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:5) · [2TI 2:23](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:23) · [TIT 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:9) · [JAS 4:1](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1)

39\.23 · Hostility, Strife · Strife, Struggle

## μεγαλεῖος (id: 003187000000000)

μεγαλεῖος
=========

μεγαλεῖος (G3167) — μεγαλεῖον

adj \| \-α, \-ον \| μεγαλύνω

76\.8 · Power, Force

mighty act, great deed a deed of importance and power In some contexts it is not possible to distinguish readily between τέρας\[b] ([76\.7](#76.7)), δύναμις\[c] ([76\.7](#76.7)), and μεγαλεῖον, for all may refer to miraculous events, and in a number of instances these terms are used in pairs, primarily to emphasize rather than to distinguish different kinds of miraculous events. All of these expressions may indicate a supernatural component with important religious implications, especially since the performance of such miracles implies divine power.

[ACT 2:11](https://ref.ly/John2:11)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 2:11

## μεγαλοπρεπής (id: 003189000000000)

μεγαλοπρεπής
============

μεγαλοπρεπής (G3169)

adj \| \-ές \| μεγαλύνω \+ πρέπει

79\.14 · Features of Objects · Beautiful, Ugly

very wonderful, sublime pertaining to being unusually attractive and beautiful For μεγαλοπρεπής as part of a title, see [12\.6](#12.6).

[2PE 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:17)

12\.6{N:001} · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

**Collocation:** μεγαλοπρεπὴς δόξα

Sublime Glory, Majestic Glory a title for God, literally: majestic glory It is rare that one can use a literal rendering of μεγαλοπρεπὴς δόξα as a title for God, since ‘Sublime Glory’ is a quality and not normally a reference to a person or supernatural being.  
It is also possible, however, to use a descriptive phrase such as ‘the one who is supremely glorious’ or ‘the one who is glorious above all others’ or ‘God who is supremely glorious.’ See [79\.14](#79.14).

[2PE 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:17)

1 Items [12\.4](#12.4)\-[12\.8](#12.8), ([12\.9](#12.9)) and [12\.12](#12.12) in this domain are titles for θεός\[a] ‘God’ ([12\.1](#12.1)). As titles, they have precisely the same reference as θεός\[a], but they each contribute distinctive meanings which are legitimate qualifications of the referent in question.

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 1:17


## μεγαλύνω (id: 003190000000000)

μεγαλύνω
========

μεγαλύνω (G3170)

μεγαλεῖον · μεγαλειότης · μεγαλοπρεπής · μεγάλως · μεγαλωσύνη · μέγας · μέγεθος · μεγιστάν · μέγιστος

79\.124 · Features of Objects · Large, Small

to make big, to make large, to enlarge to cause to be large It is possible to interpret the large size of the tassels as referring primarily to the length of the tassels and, therefore, to translate as ‘they make their tassels long.’ However, it seems more likely that the reference includes all dimensions.

[MAT 23:5](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5) · [LUK 1:58](https://ref.ly/Mark1:58) · [2CO 10:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:15)

33\.358 · Communication · Praise

to praise the greatness of to praise a person in terms of that individuals greatness In a number of languages it is necessary to restructure a statement such as ‘praising God’s greatness’ as a form of direct discourse, for example, ‘they said, God is indeed great.’

[LUK 1:46](https://ref.ly/Mark1:46) · [ACT 10:46](https://ref.ly/John10:46) · [ACT 19:17](https://ref.ly/John19:17)

87\.15 · Status · Honor or Respect in Relation to Status

to pay special respect to, to hold in high honor, to regard as important to show respect to a person on the basis of the importance of such an individual

[ACT 5:13](https://ref.ly/John5:13) · [PHP 1:20](https://ref.ly/Eph1:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:5; Luke 1:58; 2 Corinthians 10:15; Luke 1:46; Acts 10:46; Acts 19:17; Acts 5:13; Philippians 1:20


## μεγάλως (id: 003191000000000)

μεγάλως
=======

μεγάλως (G3171)

adv \| μεγαλύνω

78\.2 · Degree · Much, Little \[Positive\-Negative Degree]

great, greatly, greatness, to a great degree, intense, terrible the upper range of a scale of extent, with the possible implication of importance in relevant contexts In a number of languages the expression of intense degree associated with some activity or state is expressed by means of a verb, not an adverb, so that one may render [PHP 4:10](https://ref.ly/Eph4:10) literally as ‘I am\-intense joyous in the Lord,’ in which the form ‘am\-intense’ is an attempt to represent a verb expression in such a language.

[PHP 4:10](https://ref.ly/Eph4:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Philippians 4:10

## μέγεθος (id: 003194000000000)

μέγεθος
=======

μέγεθος (G3174)

noun \| \-ους \| μεγαλύνω

78\.2 · Degree · Much, Little \[Positive\-Negative Degree]

great, greatly, greatness, to a great degree, intense, terrible the upper range of a scale of extent, with the possible implication of importance in relevant contexts In [EPH 1:19](https://ref.ly/Gal1:19) there are two expressions of degree, ὑπερβάλλον (treated in [78\.33](#78.33)) and μέγεθος, which, though syntactically the head of the phrase, is semantically an expression of degree with δύναμις\[b] ‘power’ ([76\.1](#76.1)).

[EPH 1:19](https://ref.ly/Gal1:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 1:19

μεθερμηνεύω

μετά \+ ἑρμηνεύω

33\.145 · Communication · Interpret, Mean, Explain

to translate, to interpret to translate from one language to another In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘to translate’ or ‘to interpret’ is an idiomatic expression, for example, ‘it comes out in our language as’ or ‘in our words it means’ or ‘in our mouths it says.’

## μεθίστημι (id: 003198000000000)

μεθίστημι
=========

μεθίστημι (G3179) — μεθίσταμαι

aor. μετέστησα · ptc. μεταστήσας · aor.pass.subj. μετασταθῶ \| μετά \+ ἵστημι

15\.9 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to cause to move, to remove to cause something to be moved from one place to another It is not possible to determine whether in [1CO 13:2](https://ref.ly/Rom13:2) one should understand ‘remove mountains’ in the sense of ‘causing them to disappear’ or ‘to cause a mountain to change its location,’ that is to say, to move a mountain from one place to another.

[ACT 13:22](https://ref.ly/John13:22) · [1CO 13:2](https://ref.ly/Rom13:2)

13\.64 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Change of State

to change to, to turn into, to cause to be different from, to transform to cause a change of state, with emphasis upon the difference in the resulting state1

[LUK 16:4](https://ref.ly/Mark16:4) · [COL 1:13](https://ref.ly/Phil1:13)

31\.73 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Change an Opinion Concerning Truth

to turn away, to mislead (a figurative extension of meaning of μεθίστημι\[a] ‘to cause to move,’ [15\.9](#15.9)) to cause a complete change in someone’s beliefs, normally in the unfavorable sense of causing someone to turn away from a previous belief and hence to be misled

[ACT 19:26](https://ref.ly/John19:26)

68\.38 · (μεθίσταμαι) · Aspect · Cease, Stop

to cease to cease from a state or function, with the implication of transfer or removal See also μεθίστημι\[b] in [13\.64](#13.64).

[LUK 16:4](https://ref.ly/Mark16:4)

1 There are undoubtedly certain significant differences of meaning in this series in [13\.64](#13.64), but it is impossible to determine this on the basis of existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 13:22; 1 Corinthians 13:2; Luke 16:4; Colossians 1:13; Acts 19:26

## μέλας (id: 003203000000000)

μέλας
=====

μέλας (G3189)

adj \| μέλαινα, μέλαν · gen. \-ανος, \-αίνης, \-ανος

79\.26 · Features of Objects · Color

black, dark color Expressions for a number of terms for color differ on the basis of the object which is designated as having such a color. For example, a term for black as applied to a horse may be a different term from what one would use in speaking of a black box.

[MAT 5:36](https://ref.ly/Matt5:36) · [REV 6:5](https://ref.ly/Jude6:5) · [REV 6:12](https://ref.ly/Jude6:12)

6\.57 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

ink a dark liquid used in writing or marking The use of ink is so universal at the present time that some term or expression for it is almost inevitable in all languages. However, in some cases the equivalent is essentially a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘black stain’ or ‘writing stain.’

[2CO 3:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:3) · [2JN 1:12](https://ref.ly/1John1:12) · [3JN 1:13](https://ref.ly/2John1:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:36; Revelation 6:5; Revelation 6:12; 2 Corinthians 3:3; 2 John 1:12; 3 John 1:13

## μέλει (id: 003205000000000)

μέλει
=====

μέλει (G3199a)

ἀμελέω · ἀμεταμέλητος · ἐπιμέλεια · ἐπιμελέομαι · ἐπιμελῶς · μελετάω · μεταμέλομαι · προμελετάω

30\.39 · Think · To Think About, with the Implied Purpose of Responding Appropriately

to think about, to be concerned about to think about something in such a way as to make an appropriate response It may be possible to render ‘is God concerned about oxen’ ([1CO 9:9](https://ref.ly/Rom9:9)) as ‘is God thinking about doing something about oxen.’

25\.223 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

to be of concern, to be anxious about to be particularly concerned about something, with the implication of some apprehension In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘to be concerned about’ may be simply ‘to think about,’ and the negative might be merely ‘not to let something enter one’s head.’

## μελετάω (id: 003206000000000)

μελετάω
=======

μελετάω (G3191)

μέλει

30\.20 · Think · To Think, Thought

to ponder, to let one’s mind dwell on, to keep thinking about, to fix one’s attention on to keep on giving serious consideration to something It is also possible to understand μελετάω in [1TI 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:15) as meaning ‘to do’ or ‘to practice,’ as noted in [68\.20](#68.20).

[1TI 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:15)

30\.60 · Think · To Intend, To Purpose, To Plan

to plan to act, to plot to think seriously about a particular course of action

[ACT 4:25](https://ref.ly/John4:25)

68\.20 · Aspect · Continue

to practice, to continue to do, to cultivate to continue to perform certain activities with care and concern The construction in [1TI 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:15), in which ταῦτα μελέτα and ἐν τούτοις ἴσθι appear to be essentially synonymous reinforcements one of the other, would appear to fully justify combining these expressions as essentially equivalent in meaning, but for another interpretation of μελετάω in [1TI 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:15), see [30\.20](#30.20).

[1TI 4:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:15)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 4:15; Acts 4:25


## μέλι (id: 003207000000000)

μέλι
====

μέλι (G3192)

noun \| \-ιτος \| μελίσσιος

5\.20 · Foods and Condiments · Food

honey a sweet substance produced by bees from flower nectar Though honey may be regarded by some as a vegetable product, since flowers constitute its source, it is more specifically associated with bees and in some languages is actually called bee urine.  
μέλι ἄγριον, literally ‘wild honey,’ refers to bee honey gathered in the fields and not the result of keeping bees in hives.  
In the ancient world bee keeping was a highly developed industry, since honey was a principal source of sweetening. The equivalent of wild honey in a number of languages is ‘forest honey’ or ‘tree honey.’

[MAT 3:4](https://ref.ly/Matt3:4) · [MRK 1:6](https://ref.ly/Matt1:6) · [REV 10:9](https://ref.ly/Jude10:9) · [REV 10:10](https://ref.ly/Jude10:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:4; Mark 1:6; Revelation 10:9; Revelation 10:10

3:2](https://ref.ly/Jude3:2) · [REV 3:10](https://ref.ly/Jude3:10) · [REV 3:16](https://ref.ly/Jude3:16) · [REV 6:11](https://ref.ly/Jude6:11) · [REV 8:13](https://ref.ly/Jude8:13) · [REV 10:4](https://ref.ly/Jude10:4) · [REV 10:7](https://ref.ly/Jude10:7) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4) · [REV 12:5](https://ref.ly/Jude12:5) · [REV 17:8](https://ref.ly/Jude17:8)

71\.36 · Mode · Necessary, Unnecessary

must be, has to be to be inevitable, with respect to future developments In a number of languages there is a problem involved in speaking of what is necessary or inevitable in the future, for a distinction is made between that which is purely impersonal or physical and that which is the result of some person’s purpose, intent, or activity. As in the case of δεῖ in [MRK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Matt13:7) ([71\.34](#71.34)), it is impossible in the case of μέλλω in [MAT 17:12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:12) to determine whether the reference is merely to an inevitable future event (‘bound to happen’) or whether this is part of the plan and purpose of God. In order to avoid a wrong interpretation of [MAT 17:12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:12), it may therefore be useful to translate as ‘in the same way the Son of Man will most certainly be mistreated by them.’

[MAT 17:12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:12) · [MAT 17:22](https://ref.ly/Matt17:22) · [MRK 10:32](https://ref.ly/Matt10:32) · [LUK 9:31](https://ref.ly/Mark9:31) · [ACT 26:22](https://ref.ly/John26:22) · [ROM 8:13](https://ref.ly/Acts8:13)

67\.121 · Time · Duration of Time with Reference to Some Point of Time: Until, Delay, Still, From

to wait, to delay to extend time unduly, with the implication of lack of decision

[ACT 22:16](https://ref.ly/John22:16)

## μέλος (id: 003211000000000)

μέλος
=====

μέλος (G3196)

noun \| \-ους

8\.9 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

body part, member a part of the body1 In some languages an equivalent of μέλος is simply ‘division,’ and in a few languages an even more generic expression such as ‘things’ is used, so that ‘the parts of the body’ may be rendered by an expression meaning literally ‘things of the body.’  
In different languages the various parts of the body are classified in a number of diverse ways. In some languages the sensory organs of seeing, hearing, smelling, and tasting (those related to the head) are often set off from other types of organs, while in other languages special terms may be employed for those organs involving movement, for example, the joints, arms, legs, etc. Other languages make extensive subclassifications of body parts on the basis of whether they are external or internal, though such classifications often appear to be arbitrary, since teeth and tongue may be regarded as either external or internal.

[MAT 5:29](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29) · [MAT 5:30](https://ref.ly/Matt5:30) · [ROM 6:13](https://ref.ly/Acts6:13) · [ROM 6:13](https://ref.ly/Acts6:13) · [ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) · [ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) · [ROM 7:5](https://ref.ly/Acts7:5) · [ROM 7:23](https://ref.ly/Acts7:23) · [ROM 7:23](https://ref.ly/Acts7:23) · [ROM 12:4](https://ref.ly/Acts12:4) · [ROM 12:4](https://ref.ly/Acts12:4) · [1CO 12:12](https://ref.ly/Rom12:12) · [1CO 12:12](https://ref.ly/Rom12:12) · [1CO 12:14](https://ref.ly/Rom12:14) · [1CO 12:18](https://ref.ly/Rom12:18) · [1CO 12:19](https://ref.ly/Rom12:19) · [1CO 12:20](https://ref.ly/Rom12:20) · [1CO 12:22](https://ref.ly/Rom12:22) · [COL 3:5](https://ref.ly/Phil3:5) · [JAS 3:5](https://ref.ly/Heb3:5) · [JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6) · [JAS 4:1](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1)

63\.17 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Part

member (based on the figure of the relationship of parts to the body) a part as a member of a unit

[ROM 12:5](https://ref.ly/Acts12:5) · [1CO 6:15](https://ref.ly/Rom6:15) · [1CO 6:15](https://ref.ly/Rom6:15) · [1CO 6:15](https://ref.ly/Rom6:15) · [1CO 12:25](https://ref.ly/Rom12:25) · [1CO 12:26](https://ref.ly/Rom12:26) · [1CO 12:26](https://ref.ly/Rom12:26) · [1CO 12:26](https://ref.ly/Rom12:26) · [1CO 12:26](https://ref.ly/Rom12:26) · [1CO 12:27](https://ref.ly/Rom12:27) · [EPH 4:25](https://ref.ly/Gal4:25) · [EPH 5:30](https://ref.ly/Gal5:30) · [JAS 4:1](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1)

1 One may also classify the meaning of μελος in Domain 63 Whole, Unite, Part, Divide and consider its reference to body parts as only an instance of an even more generic meaning, namely, part ([63\.17](#63.17)). On the other hand, its frequent association wit the body in absolute contexts may justify its classification here as a generic for body parts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:29; Matthew 5:30; Romans 6:13; Romans 6:19; Romans 7:5; Romans 7:23; Romans 12:4; 1 Corinthians 12:12; 1 Corinthians 12:14; 1 Corinthians 12:18; 1 Corinthians 12:19; 1 Corinthians 12:20; 1 Corinthians 12:22; Colossians 3:5; James 3:5; James 3:6; James 4:1; Romans 12:5; 1 Corinthians 6:15; 1 Corinthians 12:25; 1 Corinthians 12:26; 1 Corinthians 12:27; Ephesians 4:25; Ephesians 5:30

## μεμβράνα (id: 003214000000000)

μεμβράνα
========

μεμβράνα (G3200)

noun \| \-ης

6\.59 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

parchment, books made of parchment a sheet of specially prepared animal skin on which one could write with pen and ink; books or scrolls made of such skin In [2TI 4:13](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:13) the reference may be to documents written on parchment or to blank sheets of parchment. Sheets of parchment were either sewn together in long scrolls or, in later developments, bound together into book form (see [6\.66](#6.66)).

89\.136 · Relations · Contrast

## μέριμνα (id: 003224000000000)

μέριμνα
=======

μέριμνα (G3308)

noun \| \-ης \| μεριμνάω

25\.224 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

anxiety, worry, anxious concern a feeling of apprehension or distress in view of possible danger or misfortune For μέριμνα as part of an idiom in [1PE 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jas5:7), see [25\.250](#25.250).  
The term μέριμνα may refer to either unnecessary worry or legitimate concern. The equivalent of ‘worry’ may be expressed in some languages in an idiomatic manner, for example, ‘to be killed by one’s mind’ or ‘to be pained by thinking.’

[MAT 13:22](https://ref.ly/Matt13:22) · [MRK 4:19](https://ref.ly/Matt4:19) · [LUK 8:14](https://ref.ly/Mark8:14) · [LUK 21:34](https://ref.ly/Mark21:34) · [2CO 11:28](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:28) · [1PE 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jas5:7)1

25\.250 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

**Collocation:** τὴν μέριμναν ἐπιρίπτω ἐπί

to put one’s cares upon, to leave one’s worries to (an idiom, literally: to cast cares upon) to stop worrying and to put one’s trust in someone For another explanation of this expression in [1PE 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jas5:7), taking only ἐπιρίπτω ἐπί as an idiom, see [90\.18](#90.18).

[1PE 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jas5:7)1

1 1PE 5:7 It is possible to interpret μέριμνα in [1PE 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jas5:7) as being the context of what one worries about.

## μερίς (id: 003226000000000)

μερίς

μερίς (G3310)

noun \| \-ίδος \| μερίζω

63\.13 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Part

share, portion part or portion, with the possible implication of a division or significant distinction

1\.85 · Geographical Objects and Features · Governmental Administrative Areas

district an administrative district In [ACT 16:12](https://ref.ly/John16:12) (the only occurrence of μερίς\[b] in the NT) the Greek New Testament published by the United Bible Societies has adopted a conjectural emendation, since the more traditional text, πρώτη τῆς μερίδος, literally ‘first of the district,’ is not only misleading in meaning but does not reflect the historical fact that Philippi was a city in one of the four districts of Macedonia but was not a capital city.

## μέρος (id: 003229000000000)

μέρος

79\.108 · ((ους n, always plural)) · Features of Objects · Shapes

side an area at the side of an object

[JHN 21:6](https://ref.ly/Luke21:6)

1\.79 · ((ους n, always plural)) · Geographical Objects and Features · Sociopolitical Areas

region, territory, land, district (though this might imply too precisely a governmental area) region or regions of the earth, normally in relation to some ethnic group or geographical center, but not necessarily constituting a unit of governmental administration1 The meanings of γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμαὅριον, and μέρος\[c] are not to be regarded as completely synonymous, but in certain of their NT usages they are largely overlapping in reference.

[MAT 2:22](https://ref.ly/Matt2:22) · [MAT 15:21](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21) · [MAT 16:13](https://ref.ly/Matt16:13) · [MRK 8:10](https://ref.ly/Matt8:10) · [ACT 2:10](https://ref.ly/John2:10) · [ACT 19:1](https://ref.ly/John19:1) · [ACT 20:2](https://ref.ly/John20:2) · [EPH 4:9](https://ref.ly/Gal4:9)

11\.8 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · General

party, group a group of people having specific membership and forming a part of a larger constituency In the NT μέρος\[d] occurs only in the expression μέρος τῶν Φαρισαίων the party of the Pharisees, and though the Pharisees constituted a socio\-religious group, the use of μέρος\[d] does not focus upon this socio\-religious aspect of the Pharisees relationship to the Jewish nation as a whole, but merely upon their identity as a part of a larger constituency. The expression the party of the Pharisees may be rendered in some languages as the group to which the Pharisees belonged or those who were counted as Pharisees or the division called Pharisees. In selecting a word for party or group, it is important to avoid a term which would be essentially political in meaning. If there is no general term for party, it may be necessary to use one with a socio\-religious denotation, since that would be the most accurate way of identifying the Pharisees in their relationship to other distinctive groups in the Jewish nation.

[ACT 23:6](https://ref.ly/John23:6) · [ACT 23:9](https://ref.ly/John23:9)

57\.199 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Earn, Gain, Do Business

business, occupation, endeavor a particular kind of business activity or occupation

[ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27)

78\.49 · Degree · Completely, Enough \[Completive Degree]

partially, to some degree, part, partly a degree which is only part of some totality2

[1CO 11:18](https://ref.ly/Rom11:18) · [1CO 13:10](https://ref.ly/Rom13:10) · [1CO 14:27](https://ref.ly/Rom14:27)

63\.15 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Part

**Collocation:** ἐκ μέρους · ἀπὸ μέρους

being part of, as a part of, in part, partially (idioms, literally: from a part) the state of being part of something

[ROM 11:25](https://ref.ly/Acts11:25) · [ROM 15:15](https://ref.ly/Acts15:15) · [1CO 12:27](https://ref.ly/Rom12:27) · [1CO 13:9](https://ref.ly/Rom13:9) · [1CO 13:9](https://ref.ly/Rom13:9) · [1CO 13:10](https://ref.ly/Rom13:10) · [1CO 13:12](https://ref.ly/Rom13:12) · [2CO 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:14) · [2CO 2:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:5)

67\.109 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** ἀπὸ μέρους

not long, temporary, for a little while, for a while (an idiom, literally: from a part) pertaining to a relatively short period of time, with emphasis upon the temporary nature of the event or state

[ROM 15:24](https://ref.ly/Acts15:24)

1 The overlapping features of meaning in γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμα, ὅριον, and μέρος\[c] may be readily illustrated by the comparable overlapping of English terms such as region, territory, and land. For example, in the case of [MAT 15:21](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21) it would be possible to speak of the region of Tyre and Sidon, the territory of Tyre and Sidon, the land of Tyre and Sidon, and even the district of Tyre and Sidon. The English terms region, territory, land, and district do differ in certain nuances of meaning reflecting primarily supplementary components which are largely connotative. 2 μέρος\[f] is incorporated at this point in Subdomain D Completely, Enough in Domain 78 Degree, since it serves as a semantic opposite to the meanings involved in πᾶς\[c] ([78\.44](#78.44)), τέλος\[d] ([78\.47](#78.47)), and ὅλος\[c] ([78\.44](#78.44)).

## μεσημβρία (id: 003230000000000)

μεσημβρία
=========

μεσημβρία (G3314)

noun \| \-ας \| μεσόω \+ ἡμέρα

67\.74 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Units of Time: Daybreak, Midday, Midnight, Late

noon, midday the midpoint of a day In a number of languages μεσημβρία\[a] may be rendered as ‘when the sun is high’ or ‘when the sun is above one’s head’ or ‘just as the sun starts down.’ For another interpretation of μεσημβρία in [ACT 8:26](https://ref.ly/John8:26), see [82\.4](#82.4).

[ACT 8:26](https://ref.ly/John8:26) · [ACT 22:6](https://ref.ly/John22:6)

82\.4 · Spacial Orientations · North, South, East, West

south It is also possible to interpret κατὰ μεσημβρίαν in [ACT 8:26](https://ref.ly/John8:26) as meaning ‘about noon,’ since μεσημβρία is a normal expression for ‘midday’ or ‘noon’ (see [67\.74](#67.74)). See also the discussion at [82\.3](#82.3).

[ACT 8:26](https://ref.ly/John8:26)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 8:26; Acts 22:6


## μεσιτεύω (id: 003231000000000)

μεσιτεύω
========

μεσιτεύω (G3315)

μεσόω

31\.21 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Agree, Consent

to bring about an agreement, to cause an agreement to bring about a mutually accepted agreement between two or more parties, with the probable additional component of making something certain Since one who was a μεσίτης ([31\.22](#31.22)) often acted as one who provided the surety or guarantee of an agreement or arrangement, there is a significant component of certainty involved in μεσιτεύω. Hence, one may understand this as implying not only the agreement but the guarantee of its validity.

[HEB 6:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:17)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 6:17

40\.6 · Reconciliation, Forgiveness · Reconciliation

mediator, one who reconciles a person who acts as a mediator in bringing about reconciliation1 A mediator may be spoken of in a number of different ways, often idiomatically, for example, ‘one who stands in the middle,’ ‘one who speaks to both,’ ‘one who cuts palavers,’ or ‘one who causes arguments to cease.’ It is also possible, however, to regard μεσίτης as being related to the process of causing agreement between the parties in question. For this aspect of the meaning of μεσίτης, see [31\.22](#31.22).

[1TI 2:5](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:5)

1 Though in μεσίτης\[b] there is an important aspect of communication, the focal feature is not primarily communication but reconciliation, and accordingly μεσίτης\[b] is considered in this subdomain rather than in one of the subdomains of Domain 33 Communication.

For example, πρός\[d] may suggest some kind of interaction or response and παρά\[b] may focus upon association, but it is difficult, if not impossible, on the basis of existing contexts to define precisely the differences in meaning. 2 1TH 2:7 One can perhaps best interpret the relationship between ἐν and μέσῳ in the phrase ἐν μέσῳ in [1TH 2:7](https://ref.ly/Col2:7) as one of redundant reinforcing, since ἐν can also be understood in the sense of ‘among,’ with.’ 3 In some contexts the meanings of μέσος\[a] ([83\.9](#83.9)) and μέσος\[b] ([83\.10](#83.10)) may be said to overlap, or the situation may be such as to provide two different interpretations. For example, in [MAT 10:16](https://ref.ly/Matt10:16) ‘sheep in the midst of wolves’ may mean that the sheep are completely surrounded by wolves or that the wolves intermingle with the sheep.

## Μεσσίας (id: 003239000000000)

Μεσσίας
=======

Μεσσίας (G3323)

noun nom \| \-ου

53\.82 · Religious Activities · Roles and Functions

Christ, Messiah (literally: one who has been anointed) in the NT, titles for Jesus as the Messiah, but in many contexts, and especially without an article, Χριστός becomes a part of the name of Jesus; see [93\.387](#93.387)) In a number of languages Χριστός (or Μεσσίας) as a reference to the Messiah occurs in a transliterated form based either on Χριστός in Greek or on Messiah in Hebrew. However, in some languages an attempt is made to represent the significance of the terms Χριστός and Μεσσίας by translating ‘God’s appointed one’ or ‘God’s specially chosen one’ or ‘the expected one,’ in the sense of one to whom everyone was looking for help and deliverance.

## μεστός (id: 003240000000000)

μεστός
======

μεστός (G3324)

adj \| \-ή, \-όν \| μεστόω

59\.39 · Quantity · Full, Empty

very full pertaining to a quantity that fills a space beyond expectations or appropriateness

[JHN 19:29](https://ref.ly/Luke19:29) · [JHN 19:29](https://ref.ly/Luke19:29) · [JHN 21:11](https://ref.ly/Luke21:11) · [JAS 3:8](https://ref.ly/Heb3:8)

78\.45 · Degree · Completely, Enough \[Completive Degree]

full of, completely, very, totally a degree of completeness, with the implication of abundance In a number of languages it is simply not possible to speak of a person being ‘full of’ some quality or ‘full of’ some type of activity. Accordingly, one must often restructure the semantic relationships so as to indicate that one is ‘completely’ of a certain nature or ‘entirely’ engaged in some activity. In fact, in some languages this may be expressed negatively in the case of [MAT 23:28](https://ref.ly/Matt23:28) as ‘within there is nothing but hypocrisy and lawlessness.’ In the case of [JAS 3:17](https://ref.ly/Heb3:17) one can often express the meaning in terms of habitual activity, for example, ‘always merciful and doing good things.’

[MAT 23:28](https://ref.ly/Matt23:28) · [JAS 3:17](https://ref.ly/Heb3:17)

68\.77 · Aspect · Do Intensely or Extensively

to be full of, to be constantly engaged in pertaining to being extensively engaged in some activity or attitude

[ROM 1:29](https://ref.ly/Acts1:29) · [ROM 15:14](https://ref.ly/Acts15:14) · [2PE 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:14)

* **Associated Passages:** John 19:29; John 21:11; James 3:8; Matthew 23:28; James 3:17; Romans 1:29; Romans 15:14; 2 Peter 2:14


## μεστόω (id: 003241000000000)

μεστόω
======

μεστόω (G3325)

μεστός

59\.40 · Quantity · Full, Empty

to fill, to cause to bulge (derivative of μεστός\[a] ‘very full,’ [59\.39](#59.39)) to cause a space to be exceptionally full In many instances one cannot speak of persons being ‘full of new wine.’ It is, however, possible in [ACT 2:13](https://ref.ly/John2:13) to say ‘they have drunk a great deal of new wine.’

[ACT 2:13](https://ref.ly/John2:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 2:13

[MAT 25:3](https://ref.ly/Matt25:3) · [MAT 25:4](https://ref.ly/Matt25:4) · [MAT 26:47](https://ref.ly/Matt26:47) · [MAT 26:55](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55) · [MRK 14:43](https://ref.ly/Matt14:43) · [MRK 14:48](https://ref.ly/Matt14:48) · [MRK 14:62](https://ref.ly/Matt14:62) · [LUK 22:52](https://ref.ly/Mark22:52) · [JHN 18:3](https://ref.ly/Luke18:3) · [HEB 9:19](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:19) · [HEB 10:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:22) · [HEB 12:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:17)

89\.123 · Relations · Combinative Relation

with, combined with a marker of a relation in which one thing is combined with another This expression in [LUK 13:1](https://ref.ly/Mark13:1) must be understood in a figurative sense, for it refers to the act of Pilate killing the people while they were sacrificing.  
In some languages this expression in [EPH 6:23](https://ref.ly/Gal6:23) can only be expressed as ‘love and trust at the same time.’  
In [1TI 2:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:15) modesty is in a combinative relation with faith, love, and holiness and not merely with holiness. In languages in which such expressions are normally translated by verbs, one may render the final clause of [1TI 2:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:15) as ‘if she continues to trust and love and to be holy while at the same time showing modesty.’

[MAT 27:34](https://ref.ly/Matt27:34) · [LUK 13:1](https://ref.ly/Mark13:1) · [JHN 19:40](https://ref.ly/Luke19:40) · [ACT 14:23](https://ref.ly/John14:23) · [EPH 4:2](https://ref.ly/Gal4:2) · [EPH 6:5](https://ref.ly/Gal6:5) · [EPH 6:7](https://ref.ly/Gal6:7) · [EPH 6:23](https://ref.ly/Gal6:23) · [PHP 4:6](https://ref.ly/Eph4:6) · [1TI 2:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:15) · [2TI 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:10) · [HEB 5:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:7)

67\.48 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Other Points of Time: Before, Long Ago, Now, At the Same Time, When, About, After

after a marker of a point of time closely associated with a prior point of time In a number of languages there is no convenient preposition\-like word such as ‘after,’ but one can render the expression in [JHN 3:22](https://ref.ly/Luke3:22) as ‘these things happened, and then Jesus and his disciples went to the province of Judea.’

among, with a position within an area determined by other objects and distributed among such objects4

with, on the same side as a marker of association in which one party acts or exists for the benefit of another In [MAT 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) there is an implied event.

[MAT 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) · [LUK 11:23](https://ref.ly/Mark11:23) · [ACT 10:38](https://ref.ly/John10:38) · [ACT 11:21](https://ref.ly/John11:21) · [HEB 12:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:14)

89\.78 · Relations · Means

by means of, with, through a marker of means, with the probable additional implication of attendant circumstance (see μετά\[d] ‘with,’ [89\.79](#89.79)) In [ACT 2:28](https://ref.ly/John2:28) πρόσωπον is a figurative designation for the presence of a person (see [85\.26](#85.26)).

[MAT 14:7](https://ref.ly/Matt14:7) · [MAT 26:72](https://ref.ly/Matt26:72) · [ACT 2:28](https://ref.ly/John2:28) · [ACT 5:26](https://ref.ly/John5:26) · [ACT 13:17](https://ref.ly/John13:17) · [ACT 15:4](https://ref.ly/John15:4) · [HEB 7:21](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:21) · [HEB 10:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:22)

1 The semantic domains of σύν\[a] ([89\.107](#89.107)) and μετα\[a] ([89\.108](#89.108)) overlap considerably, for in a number of instances essentially the same referential relationship can be expressed either by σύν\[a] or by μετά\[a]. However, in contexts involving hostility and combat, opposing forces may be spoken of as fighting against one another with μετά\[a]. In this type of context the preposition σύν\[a] would not be appropriate, since it would suggest those fighting on the same side, not on opposite sides of the conflict. 2 Attendant circumstances are often expressed in English by participial or gerund phrases. 3 2JN 1:3 In [2JN 1:3](https://ref.ly/1John1:3) χάρις, ἔλεος, and εἰρήνη refer to the events which are experienced by ἡμῶν. 4 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions in the meanings of the terms in [83\.9](#83.9) (μέσος\[a], ἀνὰ μέσον, ἐντός\[a], ἐν\[b], μετά\[h], εἰς\[e], ἐπί\[c], πρός\[d], παρά\[b]). For example, πρός\[d] may suggest some kind of interaction or response and παρά\[b] may focus upon association, but it is difficult, if not impossible, on the basis of existing contexts to define precisely the differences in meaning. 5 NEW NOTE en

## μετάθεσις (id: 003247000000000)

μετάθεσις
=========

μετάθεσις (G3331)

noun \| \-εως \| τίθημι

15\.2 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to move from one place to another, to change one’s location, to depart, departure to effect a change of location in space, with the implication that the two locations are significantly different In view of the specific reference of μετάθεσις in [HEB 11:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:5), it is possible to speak of ‘being taken up,’ but the meaning is clearly a significant change of location from one place to another, that is to say, from earth to heaven.

## μεταλαμβάνω (id: 003251000000000)

μεταλαμβάνω
===========

μεταλαμβάνω (G3335)

aor.inf. μεμαλαβεῖν \| λαμβάνω

57\.129 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Receive

to receive a share in, to have a share of to receive as one’s share in or as one’s part of

[ACT 2:46](https://ref.ly/John2:46) · [ACT 27:33](https://ref.ly/John27:33) · [ACT 27:34](https://ref.ly/John27:34) · [2TI 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:6) · [HEB 12:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:10)

90\.63 · Case · Experiencer

to undergo, to experience to experience some event or state, often with the implication of something negatively valued1

[ACT 24:25](https://ref.ly/John24:25) · [HEB 6:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:7) · [HEB 12:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:10)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions of meaning in this series of related expressions in [90\.63](#90.63) (ἀπολαμβάνω\[e], ἐπιλαμβάνομαι\[f], λαμβάνω\[h], μεταλαμβάνω\[b]), but it is difficult to determine the precise distinctions on the basis of existing contexts. As in the case of a number of verbs which mark an experiencer relation, an equivalent translation consists simply of a passive form of a verb related to the noun complement. For example, in the case of [JHN 7:23](https://ref.ly/Luke7:23), one might very well translate ‘if a person is circumcised on the Sabbath.’

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 2:46; Acts 27:33; Acts 27:34; 2 Timothy 2:6; Hebrews 12:10; Acts 24:25; Hebrews 6:7


## μετάλημψις (id: 003252000000000)

μετάλημψις
==========

μετάλημψις (G3336)

noun \| \-εως \| λαμβάνω

57\.129 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Receive

to receive a share in, to have a share of to receive as one’s share in or as one’s part of In [1TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:3) the reference of μετάλημψιν is to the activity of eating, and therefore one may translate as ‘which God created for people to eat,’ but one should not mistake the reference of μετάλημψιν for the meaning of the term.

[1TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:3)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 4:3


## μεταλλάσσω (id: 003253000000000)

μεταλλάσσω
==========

μεταλλάσσω (G3337)

aor. μετήλλαξα \| ἀλλάσσω

57\.142 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Exchange

to exchange, to substitute to exchange one thing for another1 In rendering μεταλλάσσω in [ROM 1:25](https://ref.ly/Acts1:25) it is essential to avoid anything which might mean ‘to change something into.’ It is the substitution of one thing for another; hence, ‘exchange’ rather than ‘change’ is the correct gloss.

[ROM 1:25](https://ref.ly/Acts1:25)

68\.50 · Aspect · Cease, Stop

to cease and to start, to exchange to cease one activity and to start something else in exchange

[ROM 1:26](https://ref.ly/Acts1:26)

1 μεταλλάσσω\[a] may focus somewhat more emphatically than ἀλλάσσω\[b] on the substitution of one thing for another.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 1:25; Romans 1:26

## μετανοέω (id: 003256000000000)

μετανοέω
========

μετανοέω (G3340)

νοέω

41\.52 · Behavior and Related States · Change Behavior

to repent, to change one’s way, repentance to change one’s way of life as the result of a complete change of thought and attitude with regard to sin and righteousness1 Though in English a focal component of repent is the sorrow or contrition that a person experiences because of sin, the emphasis in μετανοέω and μετάνοια seems to be more specifically the total change, both in thought and behavior, with respect to how one should both think and act. Whether the focus is upon attitude or behavior varies somewhat in different contexts. Compare, for example, [LUK 3:8](https://ref.ly/Mark3:8), [HEB 6:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:1), and [ACT 26:20](https://ref.ly/John26:20).

[MAT 3:2](https://ref.ly/Matt3:2) · [MAT 4:17](https://ref.ly/Matt4:17) · [MAT 11:20](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20) · [MAT 11:21](https://ref.ly/Matt11:21) · [MAT 12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41) · [MRK 1:15](https://ref.ly/Matt1:15) · [MRK 6:12](https://ref.ly/Matt6:12) · [LUK 10:13](https://ref.ly/Mark10:13) · [LUK 11:32](https://ref.ly/Mark11:32) · [LUK 13:3](https://ref.ly/Mark13:3) · [LUK 13:5](https://ref.ly/Mark13:5) · [LUK 15:7](https://ref.ly/Mark15:7) · [LUK 15:10](https://ref.ly/Mark15:10) · [LUK 16:30](https://ref.ly/Mark16:30) · [LUK 17:3](https://ref.ly/Mark17:3) · [LUK 17:4](https://ref.ly/Mark17:4) · [ACT 2:38](https://ref.ly/John2:38) · [ACT 3:19](https://ref.ly/John3:19) · [ACT 8:22](https://ref.ly/John8:22) · [ACT 17:30](https://ref.ly/John17:30) · [ACT 26:20](https://ref.ly/John26:20) · [2CO 12:21](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:21) · [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) · [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) · [REV 2:16](https://ref.ly/Jude2:16) · [REV 2:21](https://ref.ly/Jude2:21) · [REV 2:21](https://ref.ly/Jude2:21) · [REV 2:22](https://ref.ly/Jude2:22) · [REV 3:3](https://ref.ly/Jude3:3) · [REV 3:19](https://ref.ly/Jude3:19) · [REV 9:20](https://ref.ly/Jude9:20) · [REV 9:21](https://ref.ly/Jude9:21) · [REV 16:9](https://ref.ly/Jude16:9) · [REV 16:11](https://ref.ly/Jude16:11)

1 Though it would be possible to classify μετανοέω and μετάνοια in Domain 30 Think, the focal semantic feature of these terms is clearly behavioral rather than intellectual.

## μετάνοια (id: 003257000000000)

μετάνοια
========

μετάνοια (G3341)

noun \| \-ας \| νοέω

41\.52 · Behavior and Related States · Change Behavior

to repent, to change one’s way, repentance to change one’s way of life as the result of a complete change of thought and attitude with regard to sin and righteousness1 Though in English a focal component of repent is the sorrow or contrition that a person experiences because of sin, the emphasis in μετανοέω and μετάνοια seems to be more specificaly the total change, both in thought and behavior, with respect to how one should both think and act. Whether the focus is upon attitude or behavior varies somewhat in different contexts. Compare, for example, [LUK 3:8](https://ref.ly/Mark3:8), [HEB 6:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:1), and [ACT 26:20](https://ref.ly/John26:20).

## μετέχω (id: 003265000000000)

μετέχω
======

μετέχω (G3348)

aor. μετέσχον · pf. μετέσχηκα \| ἔχω

57\.6 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Have, Possess, Property, Owner

to share in, to have a share of to share in the possession of something

[1CO 9:10](https://ref.ly/Rom9:10) · [1CO 9:12](https://ref.ly/Rom9:12) · [1CO 10:17](https://ref.ly/Rom10:17) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [HEB 2:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:14)

23\.2 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to eat, to eat food, to drink (normally occurring together with a term specifying the particular food in question, but also occurring absolutely in contexts relating to food; μετέχω\[b] is probably more formal than ἐσθίω\[a], [23\.1](#23.1)) to partake of or to consume food, whether solid or liquid1 In contexts in which μετέχω occurs, it may be important to select a term for the eating which will go specifically with the type of food in question. For various types of distinctions made in terms for eating, see the discussion at [23\.1](#23.1) and its footnote.

[1CO 10:17](https://ref.ly/Rom10:17) · [1CO 10:30](https://ref.ly/Rom10:30) · [HEB 5:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:13)

34\.31 · Association · Belong To, Be Included in the Membership of, Be Excluded From

to belong to to be included in the membership of a group In order to express the meaning of ‘belonged to a different tribe,’ it may be necessary to say ‘he had a different tribe name’ or ‘his tribe was different’ or ‘he was counted as a member of another tribe.’

[HEB 7:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:13)

34\.32 · Association · Belong To, Be Included in the Membership of, Be Excluded From

**Collocation:** τραπέζης μετέχω

to belong to (a religious group), to eat at the table of (an idiom, literally: to share in a table) to belong to a particular religious group as evidenced by ceremonial eating2

[1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21)

1 It is possible to interpret μετέχω\[b] as simply an instance of μετέχω\[a] to have a share in or to partake of ([57\.6](#57.6)), and in [HEB 5:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:13) μετέχων could be interpreted in this sense. In [1CO 10:30](https://ref.ly/Rom10:30), however, μετέχω may be interpreted as being used in an absolute sense and thus meaning to partake of food. But it is also possible that even in [1CO 10:30](https://ref.ly/Rom10:30) one should recognize the ellipsis of an expression for food which could be supplied from the wider context. Note that προσλαμβάνομαι occurs with specific terms for food in [ACT 27:36](https://ref.ly/John27:36), but in such contexts there is no need to assign a meaning to this verb other than the more general meaning of to take hold of (see [18\.2](#18.2)). 2 It is not possible to determine on the basis of existing evidence whether the expression τραπέζης μετέχω is a genuine idiom or a phrase which is to be taken in a literal sense as referring to the ordinance of Holy Communion in contrast to banqueting in heathen temples.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 9:10; 1 Corinthians 9:12; 1 Corinthians 10:17; 1 Corinthians 10:21; Hebrews 2:14; 1 Corinthians 10:30; Hebrews 5:13; Hebrews 7:13

## μετοχή (id: 003269000000000)

μετοχή
======

μετοχή (G3352)

noun \| \-ῆς \| ἔχω

34\.7 · Association · Associate

partnership, sharing a relationship involving shared purposes and activity In [2CO 6:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:14) δικαιοσύνη and ἀνομία refer to ‘those who do right’ and ‘those who do wrong.’ In fact, in a number of languages one can only translate this expression in [2CO 6:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:14) as ‘how can a person who does right and one who does wrong join in a partnership?’ or ‘how can one who does right and one who does wrong work together?’ In this same verse κοινωνία (see [34\.5](#34.5)) has a meaning closely corresponding to μετοχή, and similarly φῶς and σκότος refer respectively to ‘those who live in the light’ and ‘those who live in darkness,’ paralleling closely the distinction between δικαιοσύνη and ἀνομία.

[2CO 6:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:14)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 6:14

## μέτρον (id: 003275000000000)

μέτρον
======

μέτρον (G3358)

noun \| \-ου \| μετρέω

81\.1 · Spacial Dimensions · Measure, To Measure

measure a unit of measurement, either of length or volume Some languages do not have a generic term for ‘measure,’ but they may express the concept by a phrase meaning ‘how one knows how big something is’ or ‘... how long something is.’ In other words, it is necessary to use expressions involving specific dimensions.

[MAT 7:2](https://ref.ly/Matt7:2) · [MAT 23:32](https://ref.ly/Matt23:32) · [MRK 4:24](https://ref.ly/Matt4:24) · [LUK 6:38](https://ref.ly/Mark6:38) · [LUK 6:38](https://ref.ly/Mark6:38) · [JHN 3:34](https://ref.ly/Luke3:34) · [ROM 12:3](https://ref.ly/Acts12:3) · [2CO 10:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:13) · [2CO 10:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:13) · [EPH 4:7](https://ref.ly/Gal4:7) · [EPH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gal4:13) · [EPH 4:16](https://ref.ly/Gal4:16) · [REV 21:15](https://ref.ly/Jude21:15) · [REV 21:17](https://ref.ly/Jude21:17)

78\.12 · Degree · Much, Little \[Positive\-Negative Degree]

**Collocation:** ἐκ μέτρου

sparingly, in a limited way (an idiom, literally: from measure) a scalar point marking considerable limitation in the extent of some activity In a number of languages this expression in [JHN 3:34](https://ref.ly/Luke3:34) may be appropriately rendered as ‘he doesn’t hold back at all when he gives the Spirit’ or ‘he gives the Spirit in an abundant way.’

[JHN 3:34](https://ref.ly/Luke3:34)

## μέχρι (id: 003277000000000)

μέχρι
=====

μέχρι (G3360)

prep

67\.119 · Time · Duration of Time with Reference to Some Point of Time: Until, Delay, Still, From

until, to, at last, at length the continuous extent of time up to a point1 The phrase εἰ μὴ ὅταν is often translated as ‘until’ (for example, μηδενὶ ἅ εἶδον διηγήσωνταιεἰ μὴ ὅταν ὁ υἱὸς τοῦ ἀνθρώπου ἐκ νεκρῶν ἀναστῇ ‘not to tell anybody what they have seen until the Son of Man has risen from death’ [MRK 9:9](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9)), but this phrase may be analyzed as meaning ‘if it is not when,’ an expression which is semantically equivalent to ‘until.’

[MAT 11:23](https://ref.ly/Matt11:23) · [MAT 28:15](https://ref.ly/Matt28:15) · [MRK 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [LUK 16:16](https://ref.ly/Mark16:16) · [ACT 10:30](https://ref.ly/John10:30) · [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7) · [ROM 5:14](https://ref.ly/Acts5:14) · [GAL 4:19](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:19) · [EPH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gal4:13) · [1TI 6:14](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:14) · [HEB 3:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:14) · [HEB 9:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:10)

84\.19 · Spacial Extensions · Extension To a Goal

to, up to, as far as extension up to or as far as a goal2

[ROM 15:19](https://ref.ly/Acts15:19)

78\.51 · Degree · Up To, As Much As, To the Degree That \[Marked Extent of Degree]

to the point of, to the extent of, to the degree that, up to a degree extending to a particular point as marked by the context

[PHP 2:8](https://ref.ly/Eph2:8) · [PHP 2:30](https://ref.ly/Eph2:30) · [2TI 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:9) · [HEB 12:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:4)

1 ἕως, ἄχρι, and μέχρι frequently occur with a postposed marker of indefinite temporal reference: οὗ, occurring with all three markers, and ὅτου with ἕως. 2 It is probable that ἕως\[c], ἄχρι\[c], and μέχρι\[b] differ slightly in meaning, but this cannot be readily determined from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:23; Matthew 28:15; Mark 13:30; Luke 16:16; Acts 10:30; Acts 20:7; Romans 5:14; Galatians 4:19; Ephesians 4:13; 1 Timothy 6:14; Hebrews 3:14; Hebrews 9:10; Romans 15:19; Philippians 2:8; Philippians 2:30; 2 Timothy 2:9; Hebrews 12:4

28\.74 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

**Collocation:** μὴ γνώτω ἡ ἀριστερά σου τί ποιεῖ ἡ δεξιά σου

to do something secretly, to do something without letting the public know (an idiom, probably an adage or traditional saying, literally: do not let your left hand know what your right hand is doing) an admonition to do something without letting people know about it It is rare that one can preserve this idiom, since in its literal form it may seem absurd. For many English\-speaking people the meaning has already been twisted by common usage to mean ‘be sure to not let anyone know if you are performing something that is shady or illegal.’ Today’s English Version attempts to represent something of the impact of this idiom by translating “do it in such a way that even your closest friend will not know about it.”

[MAT 6:3](https://ref.ly/Matt6:3)

89\.62 · Relations · Purpose

**Collocation:** μή πως

in order that ... not, so that ... not, lest marker of negative purpose, often with the implication of apprehension

[ACT 27:29](https://ref.ly/John27:29) · [1CO 8:9](https://ref.ly/Rom8:9) · [1CO 9:27](https://ref.ly/Rom9:27) · [2CO 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:7) · [2CO 9:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:4) · [2CO 11:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:3) · [2CO 12:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:20) · [2CO 12:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:20) · [GAL 2:2](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:2) · [GAL 4:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:11) · [1TH 3:5](https://ref.ly/Col3:5)

88\.95 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sensible Behavior, Senseless Behavior

**Collocation:** μὴ ὑπὲρ ἃ γέγραπται

to act sensibly in keeping with rules, to observe rules properly (an idiom, literally: not above what is written) to act sensibly in not violating written rules and traditions

[1CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/Rom4:6)

1 οὐ\[a] and μή\[a] are lexically equivalent in meaning, but they have a syntactic distribution which may be said to give them certain distinctions in so\-called class meaning. However, since these differences are based upon syntactic distributions, such distinctions in meaning are beyond the scope of this type of lexical analysis. The form οὐ, of course, tends to occur primarily in indicative clauses, while μή occurs generally in non\-indicative clauses. 2 LUK 22:35 A question such as μή τινος ὑστερήσατε; ([LUK 22:35](https://ref.ly/Mark22:35)) actually suggests agreement with the equivalent of a negative statement, ‘you did not lack anything.’ It is for this reason that in some languages the response to this type of question is with a positive particle meaning ‘yes.’

adv \| μή \+ δέ \+ ἐγώ

## μηδείς (id: 003282000000000)

μηδείς
======

μηδείς (G3367)

adj \| μηδεμία, μηδέν \| μή \+ δέ \+ εἷς

92\.23 · Discourse Referentials · Whom or What Spoken or Written About

no one, none, nothing a negative reference to an entity, event, or state Though in English one may readily say ‘tell no one’ or ‘take nothing,’ in a number of languages the negation must be related to the verb and not to a pronominal object. Accordingly, it may be necessary to translate as ‘do not tell anyone’ or ‘do not take anything.’

6\.187 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

sheepskin, fleece the tanned hide of sheep with the hair adhering In some languages it is important to distinguish clearly between sheepskin which has the fur on it (the meaning of μηλωτή) and a sheepskin from which the fur has been removed and thus equivalent, if properly prepared, to parchment.

## μήν (id: 003290000000000)

μήν
===

μήν (G3375 · G3376)

noun \| μηνός

67\.174 · Time · Definite Units of Time: Year, Month, Week, Day, Hour

month a period of time measured by a complete cycle in the phases of the moon In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘month’ is simply ‘moon,’ so that one would translate this expression in [LUK 1:24](https://ref.ly/Mark1:24) as ‘she kept herself in seclusion for five moons.’
