## μήτι (id: 003297000000000)

μήτι
====

μήτι (G3385)

ptcl \| μή \+ τίς, τί

69\.16 · Affirmation, Negation · Markers for a Negative Response to Questions

surely not, unless a marker of a somewhat more emphatic negative response Some persons have argued that the occurrence of μήτι in [JHN 4:29](https://ref.ly/Luke4:29) is contradictory, since it would appear from the context that the individuals posing the question regarded Jesus as a possible Messiah. On the other hand, asking the question in this form would have certainly fit the circumstances in which there was strong opposition to anyone claiming that Jesus was the Messiah. This form of the question would have avoided an overt commitment, while at the same time indicating peoples evident interest and concern.

[MAT 7:16](https://ref.ly/Matt7:16) · [MAT 12:23](https://ref.ly/Matt12:23) · [MAT 26:22](https://ref.ly/Matt26:22) · [MAT 26:25](https://ref.ly/Matt26:25) · [MRK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Matt4:21) · [MRK 14:19](https://ref.ly/Matt14:19) · [LUK 6:39](https://ref.ly/Mark6:39) · [LUK 9:13](https://ref.ly/Mark9:13) · [JHN 4:29](https://ref.ly/Luke4:29) · [JHN 8:22](https://ref.ly/Luke8:22) · [JHN 18:35](https://ref.ly/Luke18:35) · [ACT 10:47](https://ref.ly/John10:47) · [1CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/Rom7:5) · [2CO 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:17) · [2CO 12:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:18) · [2CO 13:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor13:5) · [JAS 3:11](https://ref.ly/Heb3:11)

91\.9 · Discourse Markers · Markers of Emphasis

**Collocation:** μήτι γε · μήτιγε

how much more a marker of emphasis, involving some degree of contrast and/or comparison

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:16; Matthew 12:23; Matthew 26:22; Matthew 26:25; Mark 4:21; Mark 14:19; Luke 6:39; Luke 9:13; John 4:29; John 8:22; John 18:35; Acts 10:47; 1 Corinthians 7:5; 2 Corinthians 1:17; 2 Corinthians 12:18; 2 Corinthians 13:5; James 3:11


## μήτρα (id: 003298000000000)

μήτρα
=====

μήτρα (G3388)

noun \| \-ας \| μήτηρ

8\.69 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

womb the uterus For the total expression as an idiom, see [10\.45](#10.45). Rarely can one translate literally [LUK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Mark2:23) as ‘every male that opens the womb,’ since this is likely to refer to an adult male who first has sexual intercourse with a woman. The reference in [LUK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Mark2:23) is, of course, to the first male child which is born to a woman, and therefore an appropriate equivalent in many languages is ‘a woman’s first baby if it is a boy.’

[LUK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Mark2:23) · [ROM 4:19](https://ref.ly/Acts4:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 2:23; Romans 4:19

little, very little a very low point on a scale of extent In [REV 3:8](https://ref.ly/Jude3:8) it would seem that μικρός might very well be classified as indicating quantity (see [59\.15](#59.15)), but it is probably better understood as indicating the extent of a state of being powerful, expressed in a number of languages in a negative form, for example, ‘you are not very powerful.’

## μίλιον (id: 003307000000000)

81\.29 · Spacial Dimensions · Specific Measures of Length

mile, kilometer a Roman mile, consisting of a thousand paces and equivalent to somewhat less than an English mile but equal to about one kilometer and a half In translating [MAT 5:41](https://ref.ly/Matt5:41) in the metric system, it would be better to simply say ‘whoever forces you to carry his pack one kilometer’ rather than to attempt more specific distance, namely, ‘a kilometer and a half.’

[1CO 4:16](https://ref.ly/Rom4:16) · [1CO 11:1](https://ref.ly/Rom11:1) · [EPH 5:1](https://ref.ly/Gal5:1) · [1TH 1:6](https://ref.ly/Col1:6) · [1TH 2:14](https://ref.ly/Col2:14) · [HEB 6:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:12)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 4:16; 1 Corinthians 11:1; Ephesians 5:1; 1 Thessalonians 1:6; 1 Thessalonians 2:14; Hebrews 6:12


## μιμνῄσκω (id: 003310000000000)

μιμνῄσκω
========

μιμνῄσκω (G3415) — μιμνῄσκομαι

ἀναμιμνῄσκω · ἀνάμνησις · ἐπαναμιμνῄσκω · μνεία · μνῆμα · μνημεῖον · μνήμη · μνημονεύω · μνημόσυνον · ὑπομιμνῄσκω · ὑπόμνησις

29\.7 · (μιμνῄσκομαι\[a]) · Memory and Recall · Recalling from Memory

to remember, to recall, to think about again, memory, remembrance to recall information from memory, but without necessarily the implication that persons have actually forgotten In some languages the process of remembering is expressed idiomatically, for example, ‘to find one’s thoughts again’ or ‘to see again in one’s heart’ or ‘to have one’s liver repeat the words.’

[MAT 5:23](https://ref.ly/Matt5:23) · [MAT 26:75](https://ref.ly/Matt26:75) · [MAT 27:63](https://ref.ly/Matt27:63) · [LUK 1:54](https://ref.ly/Mark1:54) · [LUK 1:72](https://ref.ly/Mark1:72) · [LUK 16:25](https://ref.ly/Mark16:25) · [LUK 23:42](https://ref.ly/Mark23:42) · [LUK 24:6](https://ref.ly/Mark24:6) · [LUK 24:8](https://ref.ly/Mark24:8) · [JHN 2:17](https://ref.ly/Luke2:17) · [JHN 2:22](https://ref.ly/Luke2:22) · [JHN 12:16](https://ref.ly/Luke12:16) · [ACT 10:31](https://ref.ly/John10:31) · [ACT 11:16](https://ref.ly/John11:16) · [1CO 11:2](https://ref.ly/Rom11:2) · [2TI 1:4](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:4) · [HEB 2:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:6) · [HEB 8:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:12) · [2PE 3:2](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:2) · [JUD 1:17](https://ref.ly/3John1:17)

29\.16 · (μιμνῄσκομαι\[b]) · Memory and Recall · Recalling and Responding with Appropriate Action

to recall, to remember to recall or be aware of information, and as a result to respond in an appropriate manner (for example, punishing, helping, honoring, etc., depending upon the context) In [1CO 11:2](https://ref.ly/Rom11:2) the occurrence of μιμνῄσκομαι would seem to imply more than merely a mental state of recalling the presence of Paul in Corinth. The implication may very well be to mentioning Paul in prayer.

[1CO 11:2](https://ref.ly/Rom11:2) · [HEB 2:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:6) · [HEB 8:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:12) · [HEB 10:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:17) · [HEB 13:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:3) · [REV 16:19](https://ref.ly/Jude16:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:23; Matthew 26:75; Matthew 27:63; Luke 1:54; Luke 1:72; Luke 16:25; Luke 23:42; Luke 24:6; Luke 24:8; John 2:17; John 2:22; John 12:16; Acts 10:31; Acts 11:16; 1 Corinthians 11:2; 2 Timothy 1:4; Hebrews 2:6; Hebrews 8:12; 2 Peter 3:2; Jude 1:17; Hebrews 10:17; Hebrews 13:3; Revelation 16:19

## μίσθιος (id: 003314000000000)

μίσθιος
=======

μίσθιος (G3407)

adj \| \-ου \| μισθόομαι

57\.174 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Hire, Rent Out

hired worker, hired person (derivative of μισθόομαι ‘to hire,’ [57\.172](#57.172)) a person who has been hired to perform a particular service or work1

[LUK 15:17](https://ref.ly/Mark15:17) · [LUK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Mark15:19)

1 μίσθιος and μισθωτός involve two sets of components, one focusing upon the work which such a person does and the other upon the fact that the individual in question is paid. This means that μίσθιος and μισθωτός could justifiably be classified either in Domain 42 Perform, Do or in Domain 57\.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 15:17; Luke 15:19

## μνεία (id: 003323000000000)

μνεία
=====

μνεία (G3417)

noun \| \-ας \| μιμνῄσκομαι

29\.7 · Memory and Recall · Recalling from Memory

to remember, to recall, to think about again, memory, remembrance to recall information from memory, but without necessarily the implication that persons have actually forgotten In some languages the process of remembering is expressed idiomatically, for example, ‘to find one’s thoughts again’ or ‘to see again in one’s heart’ or ‘to have one’s liver repeat the words.’

[PHP 1:3](https://ref.ly/Eph1:3) · [1TH 3:6](https://ref.ly/Col3:6)

29\.18 · Memory and Recall · Recalling and Responding with Appropriate Action

to remember and mention, to remember to mention to recall and to respond by making mention of1

[ROM 1:9](https://ref.ly/Acts1:9) · [EPH 1:16](https://ref.ly/Gal1:16) · [1TH 1:2](https://ref.ly/Col1:2) · [2TI 1:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:3) · [PHM 1:4](https://ref.ly/Titus1:4)

1 μνημονεύω\[d] and μνεία\[b] overlap with the domain of Communication (33\), since the meaning involves not only remembering but making mention of a person in prayer. It is possible, however, that the prayer would be inaudible, that is to say, silent prayer.

## μνῆμα (id: 003324000000000)

μνῆμα
=====

μνῆμα (G3418)

noun \| \-τος \| μιμνῄσκομαι

7\.75 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

grave, tomb a construction for the burial of the dead; often a natural cave or hewn out of bedrock1 In a number of languages it is important to distinguish clearly between a grave (a hole in the ground in which a corpse is placed) and a tomb (a construction built above the surface of the ground for housing a corpse). In some contexts, however, it may be better to use a more generic expression, for example, ‘places where people are buried’ or ‘places where corpses are placed.’ In [MRK 5:2](https://ref.ly/Matt5:2) it is important to avoid a term which would designate merely graves, for the demoniac who met Jesus was not living down in graves in the ground, but had found some habitation either in burial caves or in tombs constructed above ground.

[MRK 5:3](https://ref.ly/Matt5:3) · [MRK 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5) · [LUK 8:27](https://ref.ly/Mark8:27) · [LUK 23:53](https://ref.ly/Mark23:53) · [LUK 24:1](https://ref.ly/Mark24:1) · [ACT 2:29](https://ref.ly/John2:29) · [ACT 7:16](https://ref.ly/John7:16) · [REV 11:9](https://ref.ly/Jude11:9)

1 It is possible that μνῆμα and μνημεῖον\[a] differ in meaning from τάφος in that they contain a semantic component of memorial, that is, a reminder to people of someone who has died.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 5:3; Mark 5:5; Luke 8:27; Luke 23:53; Luke 24:1; Acts 2:29; Acts 7:16; Revelation 11:9


## μνημεῖον (id: 003325000000000)

μνημεῖον
========

μνημεῖον (G3419)

noun \| \-ου \| μιμνῄσκομαι

7\.75 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

grave, tomb a construction for the burial of the dead; often a natural cave or hewn out of bedrock1 In a number of languages it is important to distinguish clearly between a grave (a hole in the ground in which a corpse is placed) and a tomb (a construction built above the surface of the ground for housing a corpse). In some contexts, however, it may be better to use a more generic expression, for example, ‘places where people are buried’ or ‘places where corpses are placed.’ In [MRK 5:2](https://ref.ly/Matt5:2) it is important to avoid a term which would designate merely graves, for the demoniac who met Jesus was not living down in graves in the ground, but had found some habitation either in burial caves or in tombs constructed above ground.  
It is also possible to translate μνημεῖα in [MAT 23:29](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29) as ‘monuments to the dead’ (see [7\.76](#7.76)).

[MAT 8:28](https://ref.ly/Matt8:28) · [MAT 23:29](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29) · [MAT 27:52](https://ref.ly/Matt27:52) · [MAT 27:53](https://ref.ly/Matt27:53) · [MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60) · [MAT 27:60](https://ref.ly/Matt27:60) · [MAT 28:8](https://ref.ly/Matt28:8) · [MRK 5:2](https://ref.ly/Matt5:2) · [MRK 6:29](https://ref.ly/Matt6:29) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [MRK 16:2](https://ref.ly/Matt16:2) · [MRK 16:3](https://ref.ly/Matt16:3) · [MRK 16:5](https://ref.ly/Matt16:5) · [MRK 16:8](https://ref.ly/Matt16:8) · [LUK 11:44](https://ref.ly/Mark11:44) · [LUK 23:55](https://ref.ly/Mark23:55) · [LUK 24:2](https://ref.ly/Mark24:2) · [LUK 24:9](https://ref.ly/Mark24:9) · [LUK 24:12](https://ref.ly/Mark24:12) · [LUK 24:22](https://ref.ly/Mark24:22) · [LUK 24:24](https://ref.ly/Mark24:24) · [JHN 5:28](https://ref.ly/Luke5:28) · [JHN 11:17](https://ref.ly/Luke11:17) · [JHN 11:31](https://ref.ly/Luke11:31) · [JHN 11:38](https://ref.ly/Luke11:38) · [JHN 12:17](https://ref.ly/Luke12:17) · [JHN 19:41](https://ref.ly/Luke19:41) · [JHN 19:42](https://ref.ly/Luke19:42) · [JHN 20:1](https://ref.ly/Luke20:1) · [JHN 20:1](https://ref.ly/Luke20:1) · [JHN 20:2](https://ref.ly/Luke20:2) · [JHN 20:3](https://ref.ly/Luke20:3) · [JHN 20:4](https://ref.ly/Luke20:4) · [JHN 20:6](https://ref.ly/Luke20:6) · [JHN 20:8](https://ref.ly/Luke20:8) · [JHN 20:11](https://ref.ly/Luke20:11) · [JHN 20:11](https://ref.ly/Luke20:11) · [ACT 13:29](https://ref.ly/John13:29)

7\.76 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

monument, memorial a monument built as a memorial to someone who has died Constructions such as those mentioned in [LUK 11:47](https://ref.ly/Mark11:47) could also serve as tombs for the individuals in question. For a discussion of μνημεῖον in [MAT 23:29](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29), see [7\.75](#7.75).

[MAT 23:29](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29) · [LUK 11:47](https://ref.ly/Mark11:47)

1 It is possible that μνῆμα and μνημεῖον\[a] differ in meaning from τάφος in that they contain a semantic component of memorial, that is, a reminder to people of someone who has died.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:28; Matthew 23:29; Matthew 27:52; Matthew 27:53; Matthew 27:60; Matthew 28:8; Mark 5:2; Mark 6:29; Mark 15:46; Mark 16:2; Mark 16:3; Mark 16:5; Mark 16:8; Luke 11:44; Luke 23:55; Luke 24:2; Luke 24:9; Luke 24:12; Luke 24:22; Luke 24:24; John 5:28; John 11:17; John 11:31; John 11:38; John 12:17; John 19:41; John 19:42; John 20:1; John 20:2; John 20:3; John 20:4; John 20:6; John 20:8; John 20:11; Acts 13:29; Luke 11:47

## μνημονεύω (id: 003327000000000)

μνημονεύω
=========

μνημονεύω (G3421)

μιμνῄσκομαι

29\.7 · Memory and Recall · Recalling from Memory

to remember, to recall, to think about again, memory, remembrance to recall information from memory, but without necessarily the implication that persons have actually forgotten In some languages the process of remembering is expressed idiomatically, for example, ‘to find one’s thoughts again’ or ‘to see again in one’s heart’ or ‘to have one’s liver repeat the words.’

[MAT 16:9](https://ref.ly/Matt16:9) · [MRK 8:18](https://ref.ly/Matt8:18) · [LUK 17:32](https://ref.ly/Mark17:32) · [JHN 15:20](https://ref.ly/Luke15:20) · [JHN 16:4](https://ref.ly/Luke16:4) · [ACT 20:31](https://ref.ly/John20:31) · [EPH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Gal2:11) · [1TH 2:9](https://ref.ly/Col2:9) · [2TH 2:5](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:5) · [2TI 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:8) · [HEB 13:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:7)

29\.8 · Memory and Recall · Recalling from Memory

to keep thinking about, to think about again and again (compare μνημονεύω\[a] ‘to remember, to recall,’ [29\.7](#29.7)) to keep on recalling and thinking about again and again

[JHN 16:21](https://ref.ly/Luke16:21) · [COL 4:18](https://ref.ly/Phil4:18) · [2TI 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:8)

29\.16 · Memory and Recall · Recalling and Responding with Appropriate Action

to recall, to remember to recall or be aware of information, and as a result to respond in an appropriate manner (for example, punishing, helping, honoring, etc., depending upon the context) μνημονεύω in [REV 18:5](https://ref.ly/Jude18:5) implies much more than God’s mental state in remembering the crimes of Babylon. The reference is clearly to God’s both remembering and punishing. Similarly, in [GAL 2:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:10) μνημονεύω refers to more than mere mental awareness of those in need, for the process of recall involves doing something about the needy (compare [29\.7](#29.7)). In a number of languages it may be necessary to make this implication quite specific, for example, ‘all they asked was that we should be concerned for the needy of their group.’

[ACT 20:35](https://ref.ly/John20:35) · [GAL 2:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:10) · [2TI 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:8) · [HEB 11:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:22) · [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) · [REV 3:3](https://ref.ly/Jude3:3) · [REV 18:5](https://ref.ly/Jude18:5)

29\.18 · Memory and Recall · Recalling and Responding with Appropriate Action

to remember and mention, to remember to mention to recall and to respond by making mention of1

[1TH 1:3](https://ref.ly/Col1:3) · [HEB 11:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:22)

1 μνημονεύω\[d] and μνεία\[b] overlap with the domain of Communication (33\), since the meaning involves not only remembering but making mention of a person in prayer. It is possible, however, that the prayer would be inaudible, that is to say, silent prayer.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 16:9; Mark 8:18; Luke 17:32; John 15:20; John 16:4; Acts 20:31; Ephesians 2:11; 1 Thessalonians 2:9; 2 Thessalonians 2:5; 2 Timothy 2:8; Hebrews 13:7; John 16:21; Colossians 4:18; Acts 20:35; Galatians 2:10; Hebrews 11:22; Revelation 2:5; Revelation 3:3; Revelation 18:5; 1 Thessalonians 1:3


## μνημόσυνον (id: 003328000000000)

μνημόσυνον
==========

μνημόσυνον (G3422)

noun \| \-ου \| μιμνῄσκομαι

29\.12 · Memory and Recall · Recalling from Memory

memorial, in memory of, something to cause people to remember (derivative of μνημονεύω\[a] ‘to think about again, to remember,’ [29\.7](#29.7)) an instrument or means designed to cause to remember In translating [ACT 10:4](https://ref.ly/John10:4) it is important to avoid implying that God had forgotten; the implication is simply that prayers and acts of charity are means by which God becomes aware and thus responds to such events.  
It is also possible to restructure the meaningful components of this statement as in the case of TEV, “God is pleased with your prayers and works of charity.”

[MAT 26:13](https://ref.ly/Matt26:13) · [MRK 14:9](https://ref.ly/Matt14:9) · [ACT 10:4](https://ref.ly/John10:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:13; Mark 14:9; Acts 10:4

34\.74 · (μνηστεύομαι) · Association · Marriage, Divorce

## μογιλάλος (id: 003330000000000)

μογιλάλος
=========

μογιλάλος (G3424) — μογγιλάλος

adj \| \-ον \| μόγις \+ λαλέω

33\.107 · Communication · Speak, Talk

hardly able to speak, having difficulty in speaking pertaining to being almost mute In translating μογιλάλος it may be necessary in some instances to use a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘when he spoke, people could hardly understand’ or ‘he spoke in such a way that people had difficulty in understanding.’

[MRK 7:32](https://ref.ly/Matt7:32)1

1 MRK 7:32 Some have interpreted μογιλάλος in [MRK 7:32](https://ref.ly/Matt7:32) as meaning ‘not able to speak,’ but the context (especially [MRK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Matt7:35)) seems to confirm the meaning of ‘to speak with difficulty’ or ‘to be scarcely able to speak.’

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 7:32

## μοιχαλίς (id: 003333000000000)

μοιχαλίς
========

μοιχαλίς (G3428)

adj \| \-ίδος \| μοιχάομαι

88\.278 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

adulteress (derivative of μοιχεύω ‘to commit adultery,’ [88\.276](#88.276)) a woman who commits adultery

[ROM 7:3](https://ref.ly/Acts7:3) · [ROM 7:3](https://ref.ly/Acts7:3) · [2PE 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:14)

31\.101 · ((ί, adjectival form)) · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Trust, Rely

unfaithful, adulterous (a figurative extension of meaning of the substantive μοιχαλίς ‘adulteress,’ [88\.278](#88.278)) pertaining to being unfaithful to one’s earlier and true beliefs

[MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MAT 16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4) · [MRK 8:38](https://ref.ly/Matt8:38) · [JAS 4:4](https://ref.ly/Heb4:4)1

1 JAS 4:4 It would be possible to classify μοιχαλίς in [JAS 4:4](https://ref.ly/Heb4:4) as being a substantive and thus having a meaning different from μοιχαλίς in [MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39), where it occurs as an adjective. However, the regular use of adjectives in the role of substantives does not warrant setting up separate meanings, especially since the adjectival form may be regarded as being attributive to a syntactically implied substantive.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 7:3; 2 Peter 2:14; Matthew 12:39; Matthew 16:4; Mark 8:38; James 4:4


## μοιχάω (id: 003334000000000)

μοιχάω
======

μοιχάω (G3429) — μοιχάομαι

μοιχαλίς · μοιχεία · μοιχεύω · μοιχός

88\.276 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

to commit adultery, adultery sexual intercourse of a man with a married woman other than his own spouse From the standpoint of the NT, adultery was normally defined in terms of the married status of the woman involved in any such act. In other words, sexual intercourse of a married man with an unmarried woman would usually be regarded as πορνεία ‘fornication’ ([88\.271](#88.271)), but sexual intercourse of either an unmarried or a married man with someone else’s wife was regarded as adultery, both on the part of the man as well as the woman. In view of the married status of the woman being the determining factor in μοιχάω, μοιχεύω, μοιχάομαι, μοιχεία, and related terms ([88\.277](#88.277)\-[88\.278](#88.278)), there is a significant contrast with πορνεύω and related expressions ([88\.271](#88.271)). πορνεύω, however, may be regarded as more generic in meaning, and thus in certain contexts including adultery.  
[MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32) is usually rendered as ‘anyone who divorces his wife for any cause other than fornication makes her guilty of committing adultery,’ presumably on the implication that she would marry someone else, as is implied in the final clause of the verse.

[MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32) · [MAT 19:9](https://ref.ly/Matt19:9) · [MRK 10:11](https://ref.ly/Matt10:11) · [MRK 10:12](https://ref.ly/Matt10:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:32; Matthew 19:9; Mark 10:11; Mark 10:12


## μοιχεία (id: 003335000000000)

μοιχεία
=======

μοιχεία (G3430)

noun \| \-ας \| μοιχάομαι

88\.276 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

to commit adultery, adultery sexual intercourse of a man with a married woman other than his own spouse From the standpoint of the NT, adultery was normally defined in terms of the married status of the woman involved in any such act. In other words, sexual intercourse of a married man with an unmarried woman would usually be regarded as πορνεία ‘fornication’ ([88\.271](#88.271)), but sexual intercourse of either an unmarried or a married man with someone else’s wife was regarded as adultery, both on the part of the man as well as the woman. In view of the married status of the woman being the determining factor in μοιχάω, μοιχεύω, μοιχάομαι, μοιχεία, and related terms ([88\.277](#88.277)\-[88\.278](#88.278)), there is a significant contrast with πορνεύω and related expressions ([88\.271](#88.271)). πορνεύω, however, may be regarded as more generic in meaning, and thus in certain contexts including adultery.

[MAT 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) · [MRK 7:22](https://ref.ly/Matt7:22) · [JHN 8:3](https://ref.ly/Luke8:3)

## μοιχεύω (id: 003336000000000)

μοιχεύω
=======

μοιχεύω (G3431)

μοιχάομαι

88\.276 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sexual Misbehavior

to commit adultery, adultery sexual intercourse of a man with a married woman other than his own spouse From the standpoint of the NT, adultery was normally defined in terms of the married status of the woman involved in any such act. In other words, sexual intercourse of a married man with an unmarried woman would usually be regarded as πορνεία ‘fornication’ ([88\.271](#88.271)), but sexual intercourse of either an unmarried or a married man with someone else’s wife was regarded as adultery, both on the part of the man as well as the woman. In view of the married status of the woman being the determining factor in μοιχάω, μοιχεύω, μοιχάομαι, μοιχεία, and related terms ([88\.277](#88.277)\-[88\.278](#88.278)), there is a significant contrast with πορνεύω and related expressions ([88\.271](#88.271)). πορνεύω, however, may be regarded as more generic in meaning, and thus in certain contexts including adultery.  
The parallel expression to [LUK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Mark16:18) in [MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32) is somewhat different: πᾶς ὁ ἀπολύων τὴν γυναῖκα αὐτοῦ παρεκτὸς λόγου πορνείας ποιεῖ αὐτὴν μοιχευθῆναι, usually rendered as ‘anyone who divorces his wife for any cause other than fornication makes her guilty of committing adultery,’ presumably on the implication that she would marry someone else, as is implied in the final clause of [MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32).

[MAT 5:27](https://ref.ly/Matt5:27) · [MAT 5:28](https://ref.ly/Matt5:28) · [MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32) · [MAT 19:18](https://ref.ly/Matt19:18) · [MRK 10:19](https://ref.ly/Matt10:19) · [LUK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Mark16:18) · [LUK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Mark16:18) · [LUK 18:20](https://ref.ly/Mark18:20) · [JHN 8:4](https://ref.ly/Luke8:4) · [ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22) · [ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22) · [ROM 13:9](https://ref.ly/Acts13:9) · [JAS 2:11](https://ref.ly/Heb2:11) · [JAS 2:11](https://ref.ly/Heb2:11) · [REV 2:22](https://ref.ly/Jude2:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:27; Matthew 5:28; Matthew 5:32; Matthew 19:18; Mark 10:19; Luke 16:18; Luke 18:20; John 8:4; Romans 2:22; Romans 13:9; James 2:11; Revelation 2:22

barely, just, scarcely, with difficulty, hardly a degree which almost equals some point on a scale of extent, but not quite1 For another interpretation of μόλις in [ACT 14:18](https://ref.ly/John14:18), see [22\.33](#22.33).

22\.33 · Trouble, Hardship, Relief, Favorable Circumstances · Difficult, Hard

with difficulty pertaining to that which can be accomplished only with difficulty Because of the complications involved in rendering the expression ‘only with difficulty,’ it may be necessary to recast the translation of [ACT 14:18](https://ref.ly/John14:18) as ‘with these words they were able to keep the crowds from offering a sacrifice to them, but it was extremely difficult for them to accomplish this’ or ‘... but they had to try very hard to keep the crowds from doing so.’ For another interpretation of μόλις in [ACT 14:18](https://ref.ly/John14:18), see [78\.41](#78.41).

## μόσχος (id: 003352000000000)

μόσχος
======

μόσχος (G3448)

noun \| \-ου \| μοσχοποιέω

4\.17 · Animals · Animals

calf the young of cattle In Greek outside of the NT μόσχος is either masculine or feminine, but in the NT the forms are either masculine ([LUK 15:23](https://ref.ly/Mark15:23)) or the distinction is not indicated by the accompanying grammatical forms ([HEB 9:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:12)).  
In languages spoken by cattle\-raising people, the major difficulty is in finding a satisfactory generic expression, since the tendency is to be very specific in matters of age, sex, color, size, etc. Under such circumstances one can only select terms with more or less generic meanings or employ more specific expressions which seem to fit particular contexts.

## μυελός (id: 003355000000000)

μυελός
======

μυελός (G3452)

noun \| \-οῦ

8\.62 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

marrow the soft material that fills the cavity in the bones There are certain problems, however, involved in the rendering of [HEB 4:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:12), for strictly speaking there is no one point at which joints and marrow may be separated. Similarly, the expression ‘to where joints and marrow come together’ seems rather anomalous, since the joints bring together various bones, but they are not joined together with marrow. This passage in [HEB 4:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:12) is essentially figurative in that it is speaking of the word of God being sharper than a two\-edged sword cutting all the way through to where soul and spirit meet, and this is described as being parallel to where joints and marrow come together. Perhaps one can best state this in some languages as ‘to where the joints and the marrow are,’ thus suggesting that part of the human body farthest from the surface.

[HEB 4:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 4:12

## μύλος (id: 003362000000000)

μύλος
=====

μύλος (G3458)

noun \| \-ου \| μυλικός · μύλινος

7\.68 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

mill a construction of two flat stones between which grain was ground into flour by rotating the top stone Some mills were relatively small and operated by hand and could well be considered as artifacts. Others, however, were quite large, and animals were used to rotate the upper stone.  
In almost all parts of the world grain is ground in one way or another. Quite frequently mills are of the same general structure as those used in ancient times, in which two relatively large, round, flat stones were placed one on top of the other, and the grain was ground between the two stones. Grain entered the mill through a round hole in the upper stone, and the flour gradually emerged from around the edges of the two stones. In other parts of the world, however, grain is prepared by means of grinding stones called metates. In still other parts of the world, a mortar and pestle are used for the grinding or preparation of grain. In most contexts, what is important is either the large size of the stones or the function of grinding grain, not necessarily the particular form. However, in contexts which speak about tying a millstone to a man’s neck (see [7\.69](#7.69)) and his being thrown into the depths of the sea, it is important to refer to relatively large stones which would cause a person to sink immediately. In such a context the use of a term for ‘mortar,’ especially one of wood, would hardly be appropriate since it would normally float. Frequently μύλος may be rendered as ‘stones for grinding grain.’ In other instances, even a more generic expression may be used, for example, ‘a large stone.’

[MAT 24:41](https://ref.ly/Matt24:41) · [REV 18:22](https://ref.ly/Jude18:22)

7\.69 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

millstone a large, round, flat stone, either upper or lower, used in grinding grain μύλος\[a] ‘mill’ ([7\.68](#7.68)) denotes a mill as a whole, while μύλος\[b] denotes only one of the large flat stones of a mill. For a discussion of some of the translational problems involved in rendering μύλος\[b] ‘millstone,’ see the discussion on μύλος\[a] ([7\.68](#7.68)).

[MAT 18:6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:6) · [MRK 9:42](https://ref.ly/Matt9:42)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:41; Revelation 18:22; Matthew 18:6; Mark 9:42

## μυστήριον (id: 003369000000000)

μυστήριον
=========

μυστήριον (G3466)

noun \| \-ου

28\.77 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

secret, mystery the content of that which has not been known before but which has been revealed to an in\-group or restricted constituency There is a serious problem involved in translating μυστήριον by a word which is equivalent to the English expression ‘mystery,’ for this term in English refers to a secret which people have tried to uncover but which they have failed to understand. In many instances μυστήριον is translated by a phrase meaning ‘that which was not known before,’ with the implication of its being revealed at least to some persons.

[MAT 13:11](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11) · [MRK 4:11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:11) · [LUK 8:10](https://ref.ly/Mark8:10) · [ROM 11:25](https://ref.ly/Acts11:25) · [1CO 2:7](https://ref.ly/Rom2:7) · [1CO 4:1](https://ref.ly/Rom4:1) · [1CO 13:2](https://ref.ly/Rom13:2) · [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2) · [1CO 15:51](https://ref.ly/Rom15:51) · [EPH 1:9](https://ref.ly/Gal1:9) · [EPH 3:3](https://ref.ly/Gal3:3) · [EPH 3:4](https://ref.ly/Gal3:4) · [EPH 3:9](https://ref.ly/Gal3:9) · [EPH 5:32](https://ref.ly/Gal5:32) · [EPH 6:19](https://ref.ly/Gal6:19) · [COL 1:26](https://ref.ly/Phil1:26) · [COL 1:27](https://ref.ly/Phil1:27) · [COL 2:2](https://ref.ly/Phil2:2) · [COL 4:3](https://ref.ly/Phil4:3) · [2TH 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:7) · [1TI 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:9) · [1TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:16) · [REV 1:20](https://ref.ly/Jude1:20) · [REV 10:7](https://ref.ly/Jude10:7) · [REV 17:5](https://ref.ly/Jude17:5) · [REV 17:7](https://ref.ly/Jude17:7)

## μώλωψ (id: 003371000000000)

μώλωψ
=====

μώλωψ (G3468)

noun \| \-ωπος

20\.29 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

wound the condition resulting from being severely hurt or wounded1

[1PE 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jas2:24)2

1 These expressions for ‘wound’ (τραῦμα, μώλωψ, πληγή\[b]) normally do not imply a mortal wound. It is possible, however, to speak of a mortal wound by the phrase ἡ πληγὴ τοῦ θανάτου as in [REV 13:3](https://ref.ly/Jude13:3), [REV 13:12](https://ref.ly/Jude13:12). 2 1PE 2:24 μώλωψ appears to be a welt or bruise caused specifically by blows or beating, but the context of [1PE 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jas2:24) appears to be highly generic.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Peter 2:24

μωμάομαι

μωμάομαι (G3469)

μέμφομαι

33\.414 · Communication · Criticize

to criticize, to censure, to find fault with to find fault with someone by implying blame

[2CO 6:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:3) · [2CO 8:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:20)

## μῶμος (id: 003373000000000)

μῶμος
=====

μῶμος (G3470)

noun \| \-ου \| μέμφομαι

79\.60 · Features of Objects · Blemished, Unblemished

blemish, spot, defect that which constitutes a defect or blemish, either in the physical or moral sense The context of [2PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:13) is highly figurative, and the occurrence of μῶμος may be regarded as an instance of figurative usage.

[2PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:13)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 2:13


## μωραίνω (id: 003374000000000)

μωραίνω
=======

μωραίνω (G3471) — μωραίνομαι

aor. ἐμώρανα · aor.pass.subj. μωρανθῶ \| μωρία · μωρολογία · μωρός

32\.59 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

to cause to become nonsense (causative derivative of μωρία ‘foolishness,’ [32\.57](#32.57)) to cause the content of certain thoughts to become devoid of meaning In [1CO 1:20](https://ref.ly/Rom1:20) the focus is upon the content of wisdom and nonsense, and it may be necessary to make this explicit, for example, ‘the people of the world thought that what they understood was wise, but God showed that their thoughts were foolish’ or ‘... their way of thinking was foolish.’

[1CO 1:20](https://ref.ly/Rom1:20)

32\.56 · (μωραίνομαι\[a]) · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

to become foolish, to act more foolishly (derivative of μωρός\[a] ‘unwise, foolish,’ [32\.55](#32.55)) to become one who does not employ a capacity to understand and thus acts very foolishly

[ROM 1:22](https://ref.ly/Acts1:22)

79\.44 · (μωραίνομαι\[b]) · Features of Objects · Sweet, Bitter, Tasteless

to become tasteless, to lose taste to become insipid or tasteless In [MAT 5:13](https://ref.ly/Matt5:13) μωραίνομαι is equivalent to ἄναλος ([5\.27](#5.27)), that is to say, to be without a salt taste. Pure salt cannot actually lose its taste, but the sodium chloride of impure salt can be leached out, especially in humid weather, and the remaining substance is accordingly tasteless. See also discussion at [5\.25](#5.25).

[MAT 5:13](https://ref.ly/Matt5:13) · [LUK 14:34](https://ref.ly/Mark14:34)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 1:20; Romans 1:22; Matthew 5:13; Luke 14:34


## μωρία (id: 003375000000000)

μωρία
=====

μωρία (G3472)

noun \| \-ας \| μωραίνω

32\.57 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

foolishness, nonsense, what is thought to be foolish the content of foolish thought In rendering [1CO 1:18](https://ref.ly/Rom1:18) it is important to recognize that ‘foolishness’ must be defined in terms of the relationship that it has to those who ‘are being destroyed.’ Therefore, it may be important to translate [1CO 1:18](https://ref.ly/Rom1:18) as ‘those who are being destroyed think that the message concerning the cross is nonsense’ or ‘... makes no sense’ or ‘... simply cannot be understood.’

[1CO 1:18](https://ref.ly/Rom1:18) · [1CO 1:21](https://ref.ly/Rom1:21) · [1CO 1:23](https://ref.ly/Rom1:23) · [1CO 2:14](https://ref.ly/Rom2:14) · [1CO 3:19](https://ref.ly/Rom3:19)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 1:18; 1 Corinthians 1:21; 1 Corinthians 1:23; 1 Corinthians 2:14; 1 Corinthians 3:19

33\.379 · Communication · Foolish Talk

foolish talk, stupid talk talk which is both foolish and stupid

[EPH 5:4](https://ref.ly/Gal5:4)

## μωρός (id: 003377000000000)

μωρός
=====

μωρός (G3474)

adj \| \-ά, \-όν \| μωραίνω

32\.55 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

unwise, foolish, fool pertaining to being extremely unwise and foolish In rendering μωρός in [1CO 4:10](https://ref.ly/Rom4:10) it is essential to recognize the rhetorical exaggeration. Paul is not stating that he and his colleagues actually act unwisely or foolishly, and so it may be necessary in some languages to translate ‘we are fools for Christ’s sake’ as ‘we are regarded as fools for Christ’s sake’ or ‘it might seem that we are fools in order to serve Christ.’

[MAT 5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22) · [MAT 7:26](https://ref.ly/Matt7:26) · [MAT 23:17](https://ref.ly/Matt23:17) · [MAT 25:2](https://ref.ly/Matt25:2) · [MAT 25:3](https://ref.ly/Matt25:3) · [MAT 25:8](https://ref.ly/Matt25:8) · [1CO 1:25](https://ref.ly/Rom1:25) · [1CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/Rom3:18) · [1CO 4:10](https://ref.ly/Rom4:10) · [TIT 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:9)

32\.58 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

foolish, nonsensical, to be nonsense (derivative of μωρία ‘foolishness,’ [32\.57](#32.57)) pertaining to thoughts devoid of understanding and therefore foolish Some translators have endeavored to render μωρός\[b] in the sense of 'nonsense ́ as 'that which cannot be understood, ́ but this could refer to some type of deep mystery. Accordingly, the expression 'what the world considered to be nonsense ́ can often be better rendered as ‘what the world thinks makes no sense’ or ‘what so many people think is foolishness.’

[1CO 1:25](https://ref.ly/Rom1:25) · [1CO 1:27](https://ref.ly/Rom1:27) · [2TI 2:23](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:22; Matthew 7:26; Matthew 23:17; Matthew 25:2; Matthew 25:3; Matthew 25:8; 1 Corinthians 1:25; 1 Corinthians 3:18; 1 Corinthians 4:10; Titus 3:9; 1 Corinthians 1:27; 2 Timothy 2:23

Μωϋσῆς (G3475)

noun nom \| \-έως

93\.266 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Moses the leader of the Israelites out of Egypt and the lawgiver

[MAT 8:4](https://ref.ly/Matt8:4) · [MAT 17:3](https://ref.ly/Matt17:3) · [MAT 17:4](https://ref.ly/Matt17:4) · [MAT 19:7](https://ref.ly/Matt19:7) · [MAT 19:8](https://ref.ly/Matt19:8) · [MAT 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:15) · [2TI 3:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:8) · [HEB 3:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:2) · [HEB 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:3) · [HEB 3:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:5) · [HEB 3:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:16) · [HEB 7:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:14) · [HEB 8:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:5) · [HEB 9:19](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:19) · [HEB 10:28](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:28) · [HEB 11:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:23) · [HEB 11:24](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:24) · [HEB 12:21](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:21) · [JUD 1:9](https://ref.ly/3John1:9) · [REV 15:3](https://ref.ly/Jude15:3)

33\.59 · Communication · Written Language

the Law, the Law of Moses, the Law given through Moses, Moses the Law given through Moses, as formulated in the first five books of the OT In a number of languages it is quite appropriate to refer to the writings of a person by simply mentioning the author, but in many languages this cannot be done. Furthermore, in [2CO 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:15) it may be necessary to employ an active expression, so that one must translate ‘whenever people read the laws which God gave through Moses.’ The use of Μωϋσῆς as a reference to the Law of Moses also occurs in the phrase ‘Moses and the prophets’ as a reference to the sacred writings (compare ὁ νόμος καὶ οἱ προφῆται ‘the sacred writings,’ [33\.58](#33.58)).
